     <p><b>Portugal</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[puɾtuˈɣaɫ]</a></span>), officially the <b>Portuguese Republic</b> (Portuguese: <span lang="pt"><i>República Portuguesa</i></span>), is a country on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Southwestern Europe</a>. It is the westernmost country of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Europe" title="Mainland Europe" class="mw-redirect">mainland Europe</a>, being bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west and south and by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> to the north and east. The <a href="/wiki/Portugal%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Portugal–Spain border">Portugal–Spain border</a> is 1,214&nbsp;km (754&nbsp;mi) long and considered the longest uninterrupted border within the European Union. The republic also includes the Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagos</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">autonomous regions</a> with their own <a href="/wiki/Regional_government" title="Regional government" class="mw-redirect">regional governments</a>.</p> 
     <p>The land within the borders of current Portugal has been continuously settled and fought over since <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">prehistoric times</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Romans</a> were followed by the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigothic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a>, who were themselves later invaded by the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>. These Muslim peoples were eventually expelled during the Christian <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i>. Portuguese nationality can be traced back to the creation of the First <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>, in 868. In 1139, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_Henriques" title="Afonso Henriques" class="mw-redirect">Afonso Henriques</a> was proclaimed <a href="/wiki/King_of_Portugal" title="King of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">King of Portugal</a>, thus firmly establishing Portuguese independence, under the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_House_of_Burgundy" title="Portuguese House of Burgundy">Portuguese House of Burgundy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 15th and 16th centuries, under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>, which took power following the <a href="/wiki/1383-85_Crisis" title="1383-85 Crisis" class="mw-redirect">1383-85 Crisis</a>, Portugal expanded <a href="/wiki/Western_Civilization" title="Western Civilization" class="mw-redirect">Western</a> influence and established the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">first global empire</a>, becoming one of the world's major economic, political and military <a href="/wiki/Education_superpower" title="Education superpower" class="mw-redirect">powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> During this time, Portuguese explorers pioneered maritime exploration in the Age of Discovery, notably under royal patronage of Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a> and King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I</a>, with such notable discoveries as <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>'s sea route to India (1497–98), <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a>'s discovery of Brazil (1500), and <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a>'s reaching of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>. Portugal monopolized the <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> during this time, under royal command of the <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_%C3%8Dndia" title="Casa da Índia">Casa da Índia</a>, and the Portuguese Empire expanded with military campaigns led in Asia, notably under <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a>, who was known as the <i>"Ceasar of the East"</i>.</p> 
     <p>The destruction of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Earthquake" title="Lisbon Earthquake" class="mw-redirect">1755 earthquake</a>, the country's occupation during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a> (1822), and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">Liberal Wars</a> (1828-1834), all left Portugal crippled from war and diminished in its world power.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">1910 revolution</a> deposed the monarchy, the democratic but unstable <a href="/wiki/First_Portuguese_Republic" title="First Portuguese Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a> was established, later being superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">"Estado Novo" right-wing authoritarian regime</a>. Democracy was restored after the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> in 1974. Shortly after, independence was granted to <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">all its colonies</a>, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, which was handed over to <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">China</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> This marked the end of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">longest-lived European colonial empire</a>, leaving a profound cultural and architectural influence <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Portuguese_Empire" title="Evolution of the Portuguese Empire">across the globe</a> and a legacy of over 250 million <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Portuguese speakers today</a>.</p> 
     <p>Portugal maintains a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republican</a> form of government<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-e-book_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e-book-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> and is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Developed_country#IMF_advanced_economies" title="Developed country">advanced economy</a>, a high <a href="/wiki/Living_standard" title="Living standard" class="mw-redirect">living standard</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> being also the 11th most peaceful country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> It has the 18th highest <a href="/wiki/Social_Progress_Index" title="Social Progress Index" class="mw-redirect">Social Progress</a> in the world, putting it ahead of other Western European countries like <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> It is a member of numerous international organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD" class="mw-redirect">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>. Portugal is also known for having decriminalized the usage of all common drugs in 2001, the first country in the world to do so. However, the sale and distribution of these drugs is still illegal in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p> 
     <p></p>

         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Performance"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Performance</span></a>

           <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-35"><a href="#Public_sector"><span class="tocnumber">4.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public sector</span></a></li>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal" title="History of Portugal">History of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history:_Pre-Celts_and_Celts">Early history: Pre-Celts and Celts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history: Pre-Celts and Celts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Kingdom of the Suebi</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:23.4.14_Briteiros_086_(14012393034).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg/300px-23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg/450px-23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg/600px-23.4.14_Briteiros_086_%2814012393034%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:23.4.14_Briteiros_086_(14012393034).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros" title="Citânia de Briteiros">Citânia de Briteiros</a>, in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Minho_Province" title="Minho Province">Minho Province</a>, is the best preserved 
        <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">Castro culture</a> site in Portugal.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The early history of Portugal is shared with the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> located in South Western Europe. <a href="/wiki/The_name_of_Portugal" title="The name of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">The name of Portugal</a> derives from the joined Romano-Celtic name <a href="/wiki/Portus_Cale" title="Portus Cale">Portus Cale</a>. The region was <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">settled</a> by Pre-<a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> and Celts, giving origin to peoples like the <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">Gallaeci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes</a>, visited by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect">Phoenicians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect">Carthaginians</a>, incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> dominions as <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, after 45 BC until 298 AD, settled again by <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buri_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Buri (Germanic tribe)" class="mw-redirect">Buri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>, and conquered by <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>. Other influences include some 5th-century vestiges of <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alan</a> settlements, which were found in <a href="/wiki/Alenquer_Municipality,_Portugal" title="Alenquer Municipality, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Alenquer (old Germanic <i>Alankerk</i>, from Alan+kerk; meaning <i>church of the Alans</i>)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The region of present-day Portugal was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a> and then by <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a>, who roamed the border-less region of the northern Iberian peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-Birmp1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birmp1-28">[27]</a></sup> These were subsistence societies that, although they did not establish prosperous settlements, did establish organized societies. Neolithic Portugal experimented with domestication of herding animals, the raising of some cereal crops and fluvial or marine fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-Birmp1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birmp1-28">[27]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>It is believed by some scholars that early in the first millennium BC, several waves of <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> invaded Portugal from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> and inter-married with the local populations, forming <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">different ethnic groups</a>, with many tribes.</p> 
     <p>Chief among these tribes were the <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Calaicians or Gallaeci of Northern Portugal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians of central Portugal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici of Alentejo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes or Conii of the Algarve</a>. Among the lesser tribes or sub-divisions were the <a href="/wiki/Bracari" title="Bracari">Bracari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coelerni" title="Coelerni">Coelerni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equaesi" title="Equaesi">Equaesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grovii" title="Grovii">Grovii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interamici" title="Interamici">Interamici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leuni" title="Leuni">Leuni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luanqui" title="Luanqui">Luanqui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limici" title="Limici">Limici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narbasi" title="Narbasi">Narbasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nemetati" title="Nemetati">Nemetati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paesuri" title="Paesuri">Paesuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quaquerni" title="Quaquerni">Quaquerni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seurbi" title="Seurbi">Seurbi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamagani" title="Tamagani">Tamagani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapoli" title="Tapoli">Tapoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turduli" title="Turduli">Turduli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turduli_Veteres" title="Turduli Veteres">Turduli Veteres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turdulorum_Oppida" title="Turdulorum Oppida" class="mw-redirect">Turdulorum Oppida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turodi" title="Turodi">Turodi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zoelae" title="Zoelae">Zoelae</a>. A few small, semi-permanent, commercial coastal settlements (such as <a href="/wiki/Tavira_Municipality" title="Tavira Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Tavira</a>) were also founded in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> region by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect">Phoenicians</a>-<a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect">Carthaginians</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Lusitania_and_Gallaecia">Roman Lusitania and Gallaecia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Roman Lusitania and Gallaecia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/300px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" width="300" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/450px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/600px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3676" data-file-height="2729"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Roman_Temple_of_%C3%89vora" title="Roman Temple of Évora">Roman Temple of Évora</a>, in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>, is a symbol of 
        <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>, Roman rule in Portugal.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Romans first invaded the Iberian Peninsula in 219 BC. During the last days of <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, almost the entire peninsula had been annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect">Carthaginians</a>, Rome's adversary in the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>, were expelled from their coastal colonies.</p> 
     <p>The Roman conquest of what is now part of modern-day Portugal took almost two hundred years and took many lives of young soldiers and the lives of those who were sentenced to a certain death in the slavery mines when not sold as slaves to other parts of the empire. It suffered a severe setback in 150 BC, when a rebellion began in the north. The Lusitanians and other native tribes, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Viriathus" title="Viriathus" class="mw-redirect">Viriathus</a>, wrested control of all of western Iberia.</p> 
     <p>Rome sent numerous legions and its best generals to Lusitania to quell the rebellion, but to no avail—the Lusitanians kept conquering territory. The Roman leaders decided to change their strategy. They bribed Viriathus's allies to kill him. In 139 BC, Viriathus was assassinated, and Tautalus became leader.</p> 
     <p>Rome installed a colonial regime. The complete Romanization of Lusitania only took place in the Visigothic era.</p> 
     <p>In 27 BC, Lusitania gained the status of <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a>. Later, a northern province of Lusitania was formed, known as <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, with capital in Bracara Augusta, today's <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>. There are still many ruins of castros (<a href="/wiki/Hill_forts" title="Hill forts" class="mw-redirect">hill forts</a>) all over modern Portugal and remains of <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">Castro culture</a>. Numerous Roman sites are scattered around present-day Portugal, some urban remains are quite large, like <a href="/wiki/Con%C3%ADmbriga" title="Conímbriga">Conímbriga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mir%C3%B3briga" title="Miróbriga">Mirobriga</a>. The former, beyond being one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> settlements in Portugal, is also classified as a <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Portugal" title="Monuments of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">National Monument</a>. Conímbriga lies 16&nbsp;km from <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> which by its turn was the ancient <i><a href="/wiki/Aeminium" title="Aeminium">Aeminium</a></i>). The site also has a museum that displays objects found by archaeologists during their excavations.</p> 
     <p>Several works of engineering, such as baths, temples, bridges, roads, circus, theatres and layman's homes are preserved throughout the country. Coins, some of which coined in Lusitanian land, as well as numerous pieces of ceramics were also found. Contemporary historians include <a href="/wiki/Paulus_Orosius" title="Paulus Orosius" class="mw-redirect">Paulus Orosius</a> (c. 375–418)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hydatius" title="Hydatius">Hydatius</a> (c. 400–469), bishop of <a href="/wiki/Aquae_Flaviae" title="Aquae Flaviae">Aquae Flaviae</a>, who reported on the final years of the Roman rule and arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_kingdoms:_Suebi_and_Visigoths">Germanic kingdoms: Suebi and Visigoths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Germanic kingdoms: Suebi and Visigoths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hispania_700_AD.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Hispania_700_AD.PNG/300px-Hispania_700_AD.PNG" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Hispania_700_AD.PNG/450px-Hispania_700_AD.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Hispania_700_AD.PNG/600px-Hispania_700_AD.PNG 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="2500"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hispania_700_AD.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Visigothic Hispania and its divisions in 700, prior to the Muslim conquest.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the early 5th century, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_tribes" title="Germanic tribes" class="mw-redirect">Germanic tribes</a>, namely the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> (<a href="/wiki/Silingi" title="Silingi">Silingi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hasdingi" title="Hasdingi">Hasdingi</a>) together with their allies, the <a href="/wiki/Sarmatian" title="Sarmatian" class="mw-redirect">Sarmatians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a> invaded the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> where they would form their kingdom. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Kingdom of the Suebi</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> post-Roman kingdom, established in the former Roman provinces of <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>-<a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>.</p> 
     <p>About 410 and during the 6th century it became a formally declared kingdom, where king <a href="/wiki/Hermeric" title="Hermeric">Hermeric</a> made a peace treaty with the Gallaecians before passing his domains to <a href="/wiki/Rechila" title="Rechila">Rechila</a>, his son. In 448 Réchila died, leaving the state in expansion to <a href="/wiki/Rechiar" title="Rechiar">Rechiar</a>.</p> 
     <p>In the year 500, the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> was installed in <a href="/wiki/Iberia" title="Iberia" class="mw-redirect">Iberia</a>, centred on <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>. The Visigoths eventually conquered the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and its capital city <a href="/wiki/Bracara" title="Bracara" class="mw-redirect">Bracara</a> (modern day Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>) in 584–585. It maintained its independence until 585, when it was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> following the consecutive defeats of the two last <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> kings <a href="/wiki/Audeca" title="Audeca" class="mw-redirect">Audeca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaric" title="Malaric">Malaric</a>, and turned into the sixth province of the Visigothic Kingdom of Hispania.</p> 
     <p>For the next 300 years and by the year 700, the entire Iberian Peninsula was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>, having survived until 711, when King <a href="/wiki/Roderic" title="Roderic">Roderic</a> (Rodrigo) was killed while opposing an invasion from the south by the Umayyad Muslims. From the various <a href="/wiki/Germanic" title="Germanic" class="mw-disambig">Germanic</a> groups who settled in Western Iberia, the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> left the strongest lasting cultural legacy in what is today Portugal, Galicia and Asturias.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_the_Reconquista">Middle Ages and the Reconquista</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and the Reconquista">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px"> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg/300px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg.png" width="300" height="208" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg/450px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg/600px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_750-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="827" data-file-height="574"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         The province of al-Andalus as part of the Umayyad Caliphate 720 AD.
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Al_Andalus_-_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/300px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png" width="300" height="223" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/450px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/600px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="497"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         The Caliphate of Cordoba c. 1000 at the apogee of 
         <a href="/wiki/Al-Mansur_Ibn_Abi_Aamir" title="Al-Mansur Ibn Abi Aamir" class="mw-redirect">Al-Mansur</a>.
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Today's modern day continental Portugal, along with a significant part of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, was part of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> for approximately five centuries (711 AD - 1249 AD), following the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in 711 AD.</p> 
     <p>After defeating the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> in only a few months, the Umayyad Caliphate started expanding rapidly in the peninsula. Beginning in 711, the land that is now Portugal became part of the vast Umayyad Caliphate's empire of <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>, which stretched from the <a href="/wiki/Indus" title="Indus" class="mw-redirect">Indus</a> river in the Indian sub-continent (now <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>) up to the South of France, until its collapse in 750. That year the west of the empire gained its independence under <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_I" title="Abd-ar-Rahman I" class="mw-redirect">Abd-ar-Rahman I</a> with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Emirate of Córdoba">Emirate of Córdoba</a>. After almost two centuries, the Emirate became the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Caliphate of Córdoba">Caliphate of Córdoba</a> in 929, until its dissolution a century later in 1031 into no less than 23 small kingdoms, called <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">Taifa</a> kingdoms.</p> 
     <p>The governors of the taifas each proclaimed themselves <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">Emir</a> of their provinces and established diplomatic relations with the Christian kingdoms of the north. Most of Portugal fell into the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Badajoz" title="Taifa of Badajoz">Taifa of Badajoz</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Aftasid_Dynasty" title="Aftasid Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Aftasid Dynasty</a>, and after a short spell of an ephemeral <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Lisbon" title="Taifa of Lisbon">Taifa of Lisbon</a> in 1022, fell under the dominion of the <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Seville" title="Taifa of Seville">Taifa of Seville</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Abbadids" title="Abbadids" class="mw-redirect">Abbadids</a> poets. The Taifa period ended with the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids" class="mw-redirect">Almoravids</a> who came from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> in 1086 winning a decisive victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sagrajas" title="Battle of Sagrajas">Battle of Sagrajas</a>, followed a century later in 1147, after the second period of Taifa, by the <a href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads" class="mw-redirect">Almohads</a>, also from <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">Marrakesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Al-Andalus was divided into different districts called <i>Kura</i>. Gharb Al-Andalus at its largest was constituted of ten kuras,<sup id="cite_ref-A._R._Disney.2C_p.55_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A._R._Disney.2C_p.55-34">[33]</a></sup> each with a distinct capital and governor. The main cities of the period in Portugal were <a href="/wiki/Beja_(Portugal)" title="Beja (Portugal)" class="mw-redirect">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silves_Municipality,_Portugal" title="Silves Municipality, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Silves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1cer_do_Sal" title="Alcácer do Sal">Alcácer do Sal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santar%C3%A9m,_Portugal" title="Santarém, Portugal">Santarém</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Muslim population of the region consisted mainly of native Iberian converts to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Muwallad" title="Muwallad" class="mw-redirect">Muwallad</a></i> or <i>Muladi</i>) and to a lesser extent Berbers and Arabs. The Arabs were principally noblemen from <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>; and though few in numbers, they constituted the elite of the population. The Berbers were originally from the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_mountains" title="Atlas mountains" class="mw-redirect">Atlas mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">Rif</a> mountains of North Africa and were essentially nomads. In Portugal, the Muslim population (or "<a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>"), relatively small in numbers,<sup id="cite_ref-A._R._Disney.2C_p.58_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A._R._Disney.2C_p.58-35">[34]</a></sup> stayed in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> region, and south of the <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">Tagus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A._R._Disney.2C_p.58_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A._R._Disney.2C_p.58-35">[34]</a></sup> Today, there are approximately 800 words in the Portuguese language of Arabic origin. The Muslims were expelled from Portugal 300 years earlier than in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and this is reflected in both Portuguese culture and language, which is mostly <a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_language" title="Celtiberian language">Celtiberian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_County_to_Country">From County to Country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: From County to Country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1139%E2%80%931279)" title="History of Portugal (1139–1279)" class="mw-redirect">History of Portugal (1139–1279)</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1279%E2%80%931415)" title="History of Portugal (1279–1415)" class="mw-redirect">History of Portugal (1279–1415)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Vimaraperes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vimaraperes.jpg/175px-Vimaraperes.jpg" width="175" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vimaraperes.jpg/263px-Vimaraperes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vimaraperes.jpg/350px-Vimaraperes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Vimaraperes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A monument in 
        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a> to 
        <a href="/wiki/Vimara_Peres" title="Vimara Peres" class="mw-redirect">Vimara Peres</a>, the first ruler of the County of Portugal.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>An Asturian Visigothic noble named <a href="/wiki/Pelagius_of_Asturias" title="Pelagius of Asturias">Pelagius of Asturias</a> in 718 AD was elected leader by many of the ousted <a href="/wiki/Visigoth" title="Visigoth" class="mw-redirect">Visigoth</a> nobles. Pelagius called for the remnant of the Christian Visigothic armies to rebel against the Moors and regroup in the unconquered northern Asturian highlands, better known today as the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a>, in what is today the small mountain region in North-western <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33-36">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pelagius' plan was to use the Cantabrian mountains as a place of refuge and protection from the invading Moors. He then aimed to regroup the Iberian Peninsula's Christian armies and use the Cantabrian mountains as a springboard from which to regain their lands from the Moors. In the process, after defeating the Moors in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">Battle of Covadonga</a> in 722 AD, Pelagius was proclaimed king, thus founding the Christian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a> and starting the war of Christian reconquest known in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> as the <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista Cristã</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33-36">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>At the end of the 9th century, the region of Portugal, between the rivers Minho and Douro, was freed or reconquered from the Moors by <a href="/wiki/Vimara_Peres" title="Vimara Peres" class="mw-redirect">Vimara Peres</a> on the orders of King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III of Asturias</a>. Finding that the region had previously had two major cities—<a href="/wiki/Portus_Cale" title="Portus Cale">Portus Cale</a> in the coast and <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a> in the interior, with many towns that were now deserted—he decided to repopulate and rebuild them with Portuguese and Galician refugees and other Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Vimara Peres organized region and elevated it to the status of <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">County</a>. Vimara Peres named the region he freed from the Moors, the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> after the region's major port city—<i>Portus Cale'</i> or modern <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>. One of the first cities Vimara Peres founded at this time is Vimaranes, known today as <a href="/wiki/Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Guimarães">Guimarães</a> - the "birthplace of the Portuguese nation" or the "cradle city" (Cidade Berço in Portuguese).<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/300px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" width="300" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/450px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/600px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="616"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The historical retreat and expansion of 
        <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a> in the Iberian Peninsula.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After annexing the County of Portugal into one of the several counties that made up the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a>, King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III of Asturias</a> knighted Vimara Peres, in 868 AD, as the First Count of Portus Cale (Portugal). The region became known as <i>Portucale</i>, <i>Portugale</i>, and simultaneously <i>Portugália</i> — the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup> Later the Kingdom of Asturias was divided into a number of Christian Kingdoms in Northern Spain due to dynastic divisions of inheritance among the kings offspring. With the forced abdication of <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III "the Great" of Asturias</a> by his sons in 910, the Kingdom of Asturias split into three separate kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">León</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">Galicia</a> and Asturias. The three kingdoms were eventually reunited in 924 (León and Galicia in 914, Asturias later) under the crown of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">León</a>.</p> 
     <p>During the century of internecine struggles for dominance among the Northern Christians kingdoms, the County of Portugal, formed the southern portion of the Kingdom of Galicia. At times the Kingdom of Galicia existed independently for short periods, but usually formed an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Leon" title="Kingdom of Leon" class="mw-redirect">Kingdom of Leon</a>. Throughout this period, the people of County of Portugal as Galicians found themselves struggling to maintain the autonomy of Galicia with its distinct language and culture (<a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>) from the Leonese culture, whenever the status of the Kingdom of Galicia changed in relation to the Kingdom of Leon. As a result of political division, Galician-Portuguese lost its unity when the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> separated from the Kingdom of Galicia (a dependent kingdom of Leon) to establish the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BatalhaOurique.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/BatalhaOurique.jpg/300px-BatalhaOurique.jpg" width="300" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/BatalhaOurique.jpg/450px-BatalhaOurique.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/BatalhaOurique.jpg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="271"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BatalhaOurique.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a> was a major stepping stone in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1093, <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VI_of_Le%C3%B3n_and_Castile" title="Alfonso VI of León and Castile">Alfonso VI of León and Castile</a> bestowed the county to <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Count_of_Portugal" title="Henry, Count of Portugal">Henry of Burgundy</a> and married him to his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Theresa,_Countess_of_Portugal" title="Theresa, Countess of Portugal">Teresa of León</a>, for his role in reconquering the land from Moors. Henry based his newly formed county in Bracara Augusta (modern <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>), capital city of the ancient Roman province, and also previous capital of several kingdoms over the first millennia.</p> 
     <p>On 24 June 1128, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_S%C3%A3o_Mamede" title="Battle of São Mamede">Battle of São Mamede</a> occurred near <a href="/wiki/Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Guimarães">Guimarães</a>. <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso Henriques</a>, Count of Portugal, defeated his mother <a href="/wiki/Teresa,_Countess_of_Portugal" title="Teresa, Countess of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Countess Teresa</a> and her lover <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Peres_de_Trava" title="Fernão Peres de Trava" class="mw-redirect">Fernão Peres de Trava</a>, thereby establishing himself as sole leader. Afonso then turned his arms against the Moors in the south. His campaigns were successful and, on 25 July 1139, he obtained an overwhelming victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a>, and straight after was unanimously proclaimed <a href="/wiki/King_of_Portugal" title="King of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">King of Portugal</a> by his soldiers.</p> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> period, Christians reconquered the Iberian Peninsula from <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moorish</a> domination. A victory over the Muslims at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a> in 1139 is traditionally taken as the occasion when the County of Portugal as a fief of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">Kingdom of León</a> was transformed into the independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>.</p> 
     <p>Afonso then established the first of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Portuguese Cortes</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lamego" title="Lamego">Lamego</a>, where he was crowned by the Archbishop of Braga, though the validity of the Cortes of Lamego has been disputed and called a myth created during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>. Afonso was recognized in 1143 by King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VII_of_Le%C3%B3n_and_Castile" title="Alfonso VII of León and Castile">Alfonso VII of León and Castile</a>, and in 1179 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_III" title="Pope Alexander III">Pope Alexander III</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BatalhaFacade1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BatalhaFacade1.jpg/300px-BatalhaFacade1.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BatalhaFacade1.jpg/450px-BatalhaFacade1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BatalhaFacade1.jpg/600px-BatalhaFacade1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BatalhaFacade1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Architecture" title="Gothic Architecture" class="mw-redirect">Gothic</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/Batalha_Monastery" title="Batalha Monastery">Batalha Monastery</a>. Construction started in 1385 to commemorate the 
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aljubarrota" title="Battle of Aljubarrota">Battle of Aljubarrota</a>. It was classified as a 
        <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1983.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso Henriques</a> and his successors, aided by military <a href="/wiki/Christian_monasticism" title="Christian monasticism">monastic orders</a>, pushed southward to drive out the Moors. At this time Portugal covered about half of its present area. In 1249, the Reconquista ended with the capture of the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> and complete expulsion of the last Moorish settlements on the southern coast, giving Portugal its present-day borders, with minor exceptions.</p> 
     <p>The reigns of <a href="/wiki/Denis_I_of_Portugal" title="Denis I of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Dinis I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_IV_of_Portugal" title="Afonso IV of Portugal">Afonso IV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Portugal" title="Peter I of Portugal">Pedro I</a> for the most part saw peace with the Christian kingdoms of Iberia.</p> 
     <p>In 1348 and 1349 Portugal, like the rest of Europe, was devastated by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> In 1373, Portugal made an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">alliance with England</a>, which is the longest-standing alliance in the world. This alliance served both nations' interests throughout history and is regarded by many as the predecessor to <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. Over time this went way beyond geo-political and military cooperation (protecting both nations' interests in Africa, the Americas and Asia against French, Spanish and Dutch rivals) and maintained strong trade and cultural ties between the two old European allies. Particularly in the Oporto region, there is visible <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> influence to this day.</p> 
     <p>In 1383, <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Castile" title="John I of Castile">John I of Castile</a>, husband of <a href="/wiki/Beatrice_of_Portugal" title="Beatrice of Portugal">Beatrice of Portugal</a> and son-in-law of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Portugal" title="Ferdinand I of Portugal">Ferdinand I of Portugal</a>, claimed the throne of Portugal. A faction of petty noblemen and commoners, led by <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John of Aviz</a> (later King John I of Portugal) and commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Nuno_%C3%81lvares_Pereira" title="Nuno Álvares Pereira">Nuno Álvares Pereira</a> defeated the Castilians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aljubarrota" title="Battle of Aljubarrota">Battle of Aljubarrota</a>. With this battle, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a> became the ruling house of Portugal.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joanine_era">Joanine era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Joanine era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415%E2%80%931578)" title="History of Portugal (1415–1578)">History of Portugal (1415–1578)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/170px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/255px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/340px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="1750"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> opened the sea route to India in 1498.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal spearheaded European exploration of the world and the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">King João I</a>, became the main sponsor and patron of this endeavour. During this period, Portugal explored the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, discovering several Atlantic archipelagos like the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cape_Verde" title="Portuguese Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, explored the African coast, colonized selected areas of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, discovered an eastern <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" title="Portuguese India Armadas">route to India</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil#Discovery_and_early_exploitation" title="Colonial Brazil">discovered Brazil</a>, explored the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, established trading routes throughout most of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Asia" title="Southern Asia" class="mw-redirect">southern Asia</a>, and sent the first direct European maritime trade and diplomatic missions to <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Fernão Pires de Andrade">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">Japan</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1415, Portugal acquired the first of its overseas colonies by conquering <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, the first prosperous Islamic trade centre in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. There followed the first discoveries in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" title="Atlantic" class="mw-redirect">Atlantic</a>: <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, which led to the first <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonization</a> movements.</p> 
     <p>Throughout the 15th century, <a href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_Africa#Portuguese" title="European exploration of Africa" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese explorers</a> sailed the coast of Africa, establishing trading posts for <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal#Expansion_of_the_Portuguese_empire_.2815th_and_16th_centuries.29" title="Economic history of Portugal">several common types of tradable commodities at the time</a>, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> to <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, as they looked for a route to India and its <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, which were coveted in Europe.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, intended to resolve the dispute that had been created following the return of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, which was made by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">Pope Alexander VI</a>, the mediator between Portugal and Spain. It was signed on 7 June 1494, and divided the newly discovered lands outside Europe between the two countries along a meridian 370 leagues west of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands (off the west coast of Africa).</p> 
     <p>In 1498, <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> reached <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and brought <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">economic prosperity to Portugal</a> and its population of 1.7&nbsp;million residents, helping to start the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a>. In 1500, the Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">Gaspar Corte-Real</a> reached what is now <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and founded the town of <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Cove-St._Philip%27s" title="Portugal Cove-St. Philip's">Portugal Cove-St. Philip's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, long before the French and English in the 17th century, and being just one of many <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese Colonizations of the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg/220px-Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg" width="220" height="360" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg/330px-Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg/440px-Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="733" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pain%C3%A9is_de_S%C3%A3o_Vicente4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <i>Panel of the Archbishop</i>, from the 
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Panels" title="Saint Vincent Panels">Saint Vincent Panels</a>, a magnum opus of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1500, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Pedro Álvares Cabral</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and claimed it for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Ten years later, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> conquered <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ormuz" title="Ormuz" class="mw-redirect">Ormuz</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Strait" title="Persian Strait" class="mw-redirect">Persian Strait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>, now a <a href="/wiki/States_of_Malaysia" title="States of Malaysia" class="mw-redirect">state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. Thus, the Portuguese empire held dominion over commerce in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> and South Atlantic. Portuguese sailors set out to reach Eastern Asia by sailing eastward from Europe, landing in such places as <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the island of <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Moluccas" title="Moluccas" class="mw-redirect">Moluccas</a>.</p> 
     <p>Although for a long period it was believed the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> were the first <a href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans" class="mw-redirect">Europeans</a> to arrive in Australia, evidence points to the <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_the_Portuguese_discovery_of_Australia" title="Theory of the Portuguese discovery of Australia">Portuguese discovery of Australia</a> in 1521.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Treaty of Zaragoza">Treaty of Zaragoza</a>, signed on 22 April 1529 between Portugal and Spain, specified the anti-meridian to the line of demarcation specified in the Treaty of Tordesillas.</p> 
     <p>All these factors made Portugal one of the world's major economic, military, and political powers from the 15th century until the late 16th century.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iberian_Union_and_Restoration">Iberian Union and Restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Iberian Union and Restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal's sovereignty was interrupted between 1580 and 1640. This occurred because the last two kings of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>&nbsp;– King <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian of Portugal">Sebastian</a>, who died in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A1cer_Quibir" title="Battle of Alcácer Quibir">battle of Alcácer Quibir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, and his great-uncle and successor, King <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Portugal" title="Henry I of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Henry of Portugal</a>&nbsp;– both died without heirs, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_succession_crisis_of_1580" title="Portuguese succession crisis of 1580">Portuguese succession crisis of 1580</a>.</p> 
     <p>Subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> claimed the throne and so became Philip I of Portugal. Although Portugal did not lose its formal independence, it was governed by the same monarch who governed the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> briefly forming a <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">union</a> of kingdoms. At this time Spain was a <a href="/wiki/Geographic_region" title="Geographic region" class="mw-redirect">geographic territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> The joining of the two crowns deprived Portugal of an independent foreign policy and led to its involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> between <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg/220px-Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg/330px-Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg/440px-Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="490"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Acclamation_of_King_John_IV_of_Portugal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">John II, Duke of Braganza</a> waged the 
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a> and was acclaimed King John IV.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>War led to a deterioration of the relations with <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">Portugal's oldest ally, England</a>, and the loss of <a href="/wiki/Ormus" title="Ormus">Hormuz</a>, a strategic trading post located between <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>. From 1595 to 1663 the <a href="/wiki/Dutch-Portuguese_War" title="Dutch-Portuguese War" class="mw-redirect">Dutch-Portuguese War</a> primarily involved the Dutch companies invading many Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Colonies" title="Colonies" class="mw-redirect">colonies</a> and commercial interests in Brazil, Africa, India and the Far East, resulting in the loss of the Portuguese Indian sea trade monopoly.</p> 
     <p>In 1640, <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">John IV</a> spearheaded an uprising backed by disgruntled nobles and was proclaimed king. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a> between Portugal and the Spanish Empire, in the aftermath of the 1640 revolt, ended the sixty-year period of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>. This was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a>, which reigned in Portugal until 1910.</p> 
     <p>Official estimates&nbsp;– and most estimates made so far&nbsp;– place the number of Portuguese migrants to <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Colonial Brazil</a> during the gold rush of the 18th century at 600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-ibge_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibge-48">[47]</a></sup> This represented one of the largest movements of European populations to their colonies in the Americas during colonial times.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Brigantine_and_Pombaline_era">Early Brigantine and Pombaline era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early Brigantine and Pombaline era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1640%E2%80%931777)" title="History of Portugal (1640–1777)">History of Portugal (1640–1777)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:O_marques_de_pombal,_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/220px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/330px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/440px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="851" data-file-height="1054"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:O_marques_de_pombal,_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_de_Carvalho_e_Melo,_1st_Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Sebastião José de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal">Sebastião José, Marquis of Pombal</a>, ruled Portugal during the reign of King 
        <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">Joseph I</a>, as an enlightened despot.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1738, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_de_Carvalho_e_Melo,_1st_Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Sebastião José de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal">Sebastião José de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal</a>, began a diplomatic career as the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">Ambassador</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">Queen consort</a> of Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Anne_of_Austria" title="Mary Anne of Austria" class="mw-redirect">Archduchess Maria Anne Josefa of Austria</a>, was fond of Melo; and after his first wife died, she arranged the widowed de Melo's second marriage to the daughter of the Austrian Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Josef,_Count_von_Daun" title="Leopold Josef, Count von Daun" class="mw-redirect">Leopold Josef, Count von Daun</a>. King <a href="/wiki/John_V_of_Portugal" title="John V of Portugal">John V of Portugal</a>, however, was not pleased and recalled Melo to Portugal in 1749. John V died the following year and his son, Joseph I of Portugal, was crowned. In contrast to his father, Joseph I was fond of de Melo, and with the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Mother" title="Queen Mother" class="mw-redirect">Queen Mother</a>'s approval, he appointed Melo as <a href="/wiki/Political_minister" title="Political minister" class="mw-redirect">Minister</a> of Foreign Affairs.</p> 
     <p>As the King's confidence in de Melo increased, the King entrusted him with more control of the state. By 1755, Sebastião de Melo was made Prime Minister. Impressed by British economic success that he had witnessed from the Ambassador, he successfully implemented similar <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economic</a> policies in Portugal. He abolished slavery in Portugal and in the Portuguese colonies in India; reorganized the army and the navy; restructured the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">University of Coimbra</a>, and ended discrimination against different <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> sects in Portugal.</p> 
     <p>But Sebastião de Melo's greatest reforms were economic and financial, with the creation of several companies and guilds to regulate every commercial activity. He demarcated the region for production of <a href="/wiki/Port_wine" title="Port wine">Port</a> to ensure the wine's quality, and this was the first attempt to control wine quality and production in Europe. He ruled with a strong hand by imposing strict law upon all classes of Portuguese society from the high nobility to the poorest working class, along with a widespread review of the country's tax system. These reforms gained him enemies in the upper classes, especially among the high nobility, who despised him as a social upstart.</p> 
     <p>Disaster fell upon Portugal in the morning of 1 November 1755, when <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> was struck by <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">a violent earthquake</a> with an estimated <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">Richter scale</a> magnitude of 9. The city was razed to the ground by the earthquake and the subsequent tsunami and ensuing fires.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Sebastião de Melo survived by a stroke of luck and then immediately embarked on rebuilding the city, with his famous quote: "What now? We bury the dead and take care of the living."</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755,_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png/300px-Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png" width="300" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png/450px-Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png/600px-Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755%2C_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png 2x" data-file-width="2692" data-file-height="1662"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Alegoria_ao_Terramoto_de_1755,_Jo%C3%A3o_Glama_Strob%C3%ABrle.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">Great Lisbon earthquake</a> of 1755 devastated the city and much of central and southern Portugal.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Despite the calamity and huge <a href="/wiki/Death_toll" title="Death toll" class="mw-redirect">death toll</a>, Lisbon suffered no epidemics and within less than one year was already being rebuilt. The new city centre of Lisbon was designed to resist subsequent earthquakes. Architectural models were built for tests, and the effects of an earthquake were simulated by marching troops around the models. The buildings and big squares of the Pombaline City Centre still remain as one of Lisbon's tourist attractions. Sebastião de Melo also made an important contribution to the study of <a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">seismology</a> by designing an inquiry that was sent to every parish in the country.</p> 
     <p>Following the earthquake, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">Joseph I</a> gave his Prime Minister even more power, and Sebastião de Melo became a powerful, progressive dictator. As his power grew, his enemies increased in number, and bitter disputes with the high nobility became frequent. In 1758 Joseph I was wounded in an attempted assassination. The <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1vora_affair" title="Távora affair">Távora family</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Aveiro" title="Dukes of Aveiro" class="mw-redirect">Duke of Aveiro</a> were implicated and executed after a quick trial. The <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a> were expelled from the country and their assets confiscated by the crown. Sebastião de Melo prosecuted every person involved, even women and children. This was the final stroke that broke the power of the aristocracy. Joseph I made his loyal minister Count of <a href="/wiki/Oeiras_Municipality,_Portugal" title="Oeiras Municipality, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Oeiras</a> in 1759.</p> 
     <p>In 1762, <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93Portuguese_War,_1761%E2%80%931763" title="Spanish–Portuguese War, 1761–1763" class="mw-redirect">Spain invaded Portuguese territory</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, but by 1763 the <i>status quo</i> between Spain and Portugal before the war had been restored.</p> 
     <p>Following the Távora affair, the new Count of Oeiras knew no opposition. Made "Marquis of Pombal" in 1770, he effectively ruled Portugal until Joseph I's death in 1779. However, historians also argue that Pombal’s "enlightenment," while far-reaching, was primarily a mechanism for enhancing autocracy at the expense of individual liberty and especially an apparatus for crushing opposition, suppressing criticism, and furthering colonial economic exploitation as well as intensifying book censorship and consolidating personal control and profit.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_and_Imperial_change">National and Imperial change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: National and Imperial change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1777%E2%80%931834)" title="History of Portugal (1777–1834)">History of Portugal (1777–1834)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg/170px-Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg/255px-Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg/340px-Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="511"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Joao_VI_Portugal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">John VI</a>'s reign was the first time that Portugal was a
