     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Portugal" title="Foreign relations of Portugal">Foreign relations of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/300px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/450px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/600px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2608" data-file-height="1952"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Necessidades" title="Palace of Necessidades">Necessidades Palace</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, houses the 
        <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Portugal)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Portugal)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1955, Portugal is also a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> (1949), <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD" class="mw-redirect">OECD</a> (1961) and <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a> (1960); it left the latter in 1986 to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, that would become the European Union in 1993. In 1996 it co-founded the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), which seeks to foster closer economic and cultural ties between the world's <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations.</p> 
     <p>In addition, Portugal is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a> (1983) and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a> (1949). It has a friendship alliance and <a href="/wiki/Multiple_citizenship" title="Multiple citizenship">dual citizenship</a> treaty with its former colony, Brazil. Portugal and England (subsequently, the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland) share the world's oldest active military accord through their <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">Anglo-Portuguese Alliance</a> (<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Windsor_(1386)" title="Treaty of Windsor (1386)">Treaty of Windsor</a>), which was signed in 1373.</p> 
     <p>There are two international territorial disputes, both with Spain:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">Olivenza</a>. Under Portuguese sovereignty since 1297, the municipality of Olivenza was ceded to Spain under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Badajoz_(1801)" title="Treaty of Badajoz (1801)">Treaty of Badajoz</a> in 1801, after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Oranges" title="War of the Oranges">War of the Oranges</a>. Portugal claimed it back in 1815 under the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Treaty of Vienna</a>. However, since the 19th century, it has been continuously ruled by Spain which considers the territory theirs not only <i>de facto</i> but also <i>de jure</i>.</li> 
      <li>The Ilhas Selvagens (<a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>). The archipelago is under Portuguese domination but is geographically closer to the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> (165&nbsp;km) than to <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> (280&nbsp;km). Found in 1364 by Italian navigators, the islands belonged to private owners until 1971, when the Portuguese government bought them and established a natural reserve area covering the whole archipelago. The islands have been claimed by Spain since 1911 and the dispute has caused some periods of political tension between the two countries. The main problem is not so much their intrinsic value but the fact that they expand considerably to the south the <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone" class="mw-redirect">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> of Portugal.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese Armed Forces</a>
     </div> 
     <table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px #ddd solid;"> 
      <caption>
       <b>Branches of the Portuguese Armed Forces</b>
      </caption> 
      <tbody>
       <tr style="text-align:center;"> 
        <td style="width:130px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="PoA Chaimite V-200 convoy DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG/150px-PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG" width="150" height="100" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG/225px-PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG/300px-PoA_Chaimite_V-200_convoy_DF-SD-04-08002.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="1152"></a><br> <small><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army" title="Portuguese Army">Portuguese Army</a><br> <a href="/wiki/Bravia_Chaimite" title="Bravia Chaimite">Chaimite V-200</a></small></td> 
        <td style="width:130px;"><a href="/wiki/File:POS_Corte_Real_(F_332).jpg" class="image"><img alt="POS Corte Real (F 332).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg/150px-POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg" width="150" height="100" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg/224px-POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg/299px-POS_Corte_Real_%28F_332%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a><br> <small><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Portuguese Navy</a><br> <a href="/wiki/MEKO_200" title="MEKO 200">MEKO-200 PN</a></small></td> 
        <td style="width:130px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon,_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Lockheed F-16A Fighting Falcon, Portugal - Air Force AN1088466.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg/150px-Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg" width="150" height="100" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg/225px-Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg/300px-Lockheed_F-16A_Fighting_Falcon%2C_Portugal_-_Air_Force_AN1088466.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a><br> <small><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Air_Force" title="Portuguese Air Force">Portuguese Air Force</a><br> <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16 Fighting Falcon</a></small></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The armed forces have three branches: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army" title="Portuguese Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Air_Force" title="Portuguese Air Force">Air Force</a>. They serve primarily as a self-defense force whose mission is to protect the territorial integrity of the country and provide humanitarian assistance and security at home and abroad. As of 2008, the three branches numbered 39,200 active personnel including 7,500 women. <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">Portuguese military expenditure</a> in 2009 was $5.2 billion, representing 2.1 percent of GDP. Military conscription was abolished in 2004. The minimum age for voluntary recruitment is 18 years.</p> 
     <p>The Army (21,000 personnel) comprises three brigades and other small units. An <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Intervention_Brigade" title="Portuguese Intervention Brigade" class="mw-redirect">infantry brigade</a> (mainly equipped with <a href="/wiki/Pandur_II" title="Pandur II">Pandur II</a> <a href="/wiki/Armoured_personnel_carrier" title="Armoured personnel carrier">APC</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mechanized_Brigade" title="Portuguese Mechanized Brigade">mechanized brigade</a> (mainly equipped with <a href="/wiki/Leopard_2" title="Leopard 2">Leopard 2 A6</a> tanks and <a href="/wiki/M113" title="M113" class="mw-redirect">M113</a> APC) and a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Rapid_Reaction_Brigade" title="Portuguese Rapid Reaction Brigade" class="mw-redirect">Rapid Reaction Brigade</a> (consisting of paratroopers, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army_Commandos" title="Portuguese Army Commandos">commandos</a> and rangers). The Navy (10,700 personnel, of which 1,580 are <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Marines" title="Portuguese Marines" class="mw-redirect">marines</a>) has five frigates, seven corvettes, two submarines, and 28 patrol and auxiliary vessels. The Air Force (7,500 personnel) has the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="Lockheed F-16 Fighting Falcon" class="mw-redirect">Lockheed F-16 Fighting Falcon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dassault/Dornier_Alpha_Jet" title="Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet">Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet</a> as the main combat aircraft.</p> 
     <p>In addition to the three branches of the armed forces, there is the <a href="/wiki/National_Republican_Guard_(Portugal)" title="National Republican Guard (Portugal)">National Republican Guard</a>, a security force subject to military law and organization (<a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a>) comprising 25,000 personnel. This force is under the authority of both the Defense and the Interior Ministry. It has provided detachments for participation in international operations in Iraq and East Timor.</p> 
     <p>The United States maintains a military presence with 770 troops in the <a href="/wiki/Lajes_Air_Base" title="Lajes Air Base" class="mw-redirect">Lajes Air Base</a> at <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira Island</a>, in the Azores. The <a href="/wiki/Allied_Joint_Force_Command_Lisbon" title="Allied Joint Force Command Lisbon">Allied Joint Force Command Lisbon</a> (JFC Lisbon)&nbsp;– one of the three main subdivisions of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Operations" title="Allied Command Operations" class="mw-redirect">Allied Command Operations</a>&nbsp;– it is based in <a href="/wiki/Oeiras_Municipality,_Portugal" title="Oeiras Municipality, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Oeiras</a>, near Lisbon.</p> 
     <p>In the 20th century, Portugal engaged in two major conflicts: <a href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_Great_War" title="Portugal in the Great War" class="mw-redirect">World War I</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> (1961–1974). After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> in 1975, the Portuguese Armed Forces have participated in peacekeeping missions in East Timor, Bosnia, Kosovo, Afghanistan, Somalia, Iraq (<a href="/wiki/Nasiriyah" title="Nasiriyah">Nasiriyah</a>) and Lebanon. Portugal also conducted several independent unilateral military operations abroad, as were the cases of the interventions of the Portuguese Armed Forces in Angola in 1992 and in Guinea-Bissau in 1998 with the main objectives of protecting and withdrawing of Portuguese and foreign citizens threatened by local civil conflicts.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_finance">Government finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Government finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9314_Portuguese_financial_crisis" title="2010–14 Portuguese financial crisis">2010–14 Portuguese financial crisis</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" class="image"><img alt="Portuguese debt compared to Eurozone average" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/300px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" width="300" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/450px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/600px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png 2x" data-file-width="703" data-file-height="681"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Government debt as a&nbsp;% of the national economy, compared to Eurozone average.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Portuguese government is heavily indebted, and received a 78 billion euro bailout from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-63">[62]</a></sup> The ratio of Portugal’s debt to its overall economy, was 107 percent when it received the bailout.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-63">[62]</a></sup> As part of the deal, the country agreed to cut its budget deficit from 9.8 percent of GDP in 2010 to 5.9 percent in 2011, 4.5 percent in 2012 and 3 percent in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-64">[63]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After the bailout was announced, the Portuguese government headed by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Passos_Coelho" title="Pedro Passos Coelho">Pedro Passos Coelho</a> managed to implement measures with the intention of improve the State's financial situation, including tax hikes, a freeze of civil service-related lower-wages and cuts of higher-wages by 14.3%, on top of the government's spending cuts. The Portuguese government also agreed to eliminate its <a href="/wiki/Golden_share" title="Golden share">golden share</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Telecom" title="Portugal Telecom">Portugal Telecom</a> which gave it veto power over vital decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> In 2012, all public servants had already seen an average wage cut of 20% relative to their 2010 baseline, with cuts reaching 25% for those earning more than 1,500 euro per month.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The IMF, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> (EC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> (ECB) said in September 2012 that Portugal’s debt would peak at 124 percent of gross domestic product in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-October_2012_status_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_2012_status-68">[67]</a></sup> The IMF previously said in July 2012 that Portugal’s debt would peak at about 118.5 percent of GDP in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-October_2012_status_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_2012_status-68">[67]</a></sup> In September 2013, the Portuguese Government reviewed again the public debt of Portugal for 2013 to 127.8 percent, after a peak of 130.9 percent in that month.<sup id="cite_ref-September_2013_status_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-September_2013_status-69">[68]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A report released in January 2011 by the <a href="/wiki/Di%C3%A1rio_de_Not%C3%ADcias" title="Diário de Notícias">Diário de Notícias</a><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> and published in Portugal by <a href="/wiki/Gradiva" title="Gradiva">Gradiva</a>, had demonstrated that in the period between the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> in 1974 and 2010, the democratic <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Portugal" title="Government of Portugal">Portuguese Republic governments</a> encouraged over-expenditure and investment bubbles through unclear <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public–private partnership">Public–private partnerships</a> and funding of numerous ineffective and unnecessary external consultancy and advisory of committees and firms. This allowed considerable <a href="/wiki/Slippage_(finance)" title="Slippage (finance)">slippage</a> in state-managed <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">public works</a> and inflated top management and head officer bonuses and wages. Persistent and lasting recruitment policies boosted the number of redundant public servants. Risky <a href="/wiki/Credit_(finance)" title="Credit (finance)">credit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_debt" title="Public debt" class="mw-redirect">public debt</a> creation, and European <a href="/wiki/Structural_and_cohesion_funds" title="Structural and cohesion funds" class="mw-redirect">structural and cohesion funds</a> were mismanaged across almost four decades.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>, it was known in 2008–2009 that two Portuguese banks (<a href="/wiki/Banco_Portugu%C3%AAs_de_Neg%C3%B3cios" title="Banco Português de Negócios">Banco Português de Negócios</a> (BPN) and <a href="/wiki/Banco_Privado_Portugu%C3%AAs" title="Banco Privado Português">Banco Privado Português</a> (BPP)) had been accumulating losses for years due to bad investments, embezzlement and accounting fraud. The case of BPN was particularly serious because of its size, market share, and the political implications - Portugal's then current President, Cavaco Silva, and some of his political allies, maintained personal and business relationships with the bank and its CEO, who was eventually charged and arrested for fraud and other crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> In the grounds of avoiding a potentially serious financial crisis in the Portuguese economy, the Portuguese government decided to give them a bailout, eventually at a future loss to taxpayers and to the Portuguese people in general.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Portugal" title="Economy of Portugal">Economy of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/350px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/525px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/700px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="667"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A proportional representation of Portugal's exports.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> in northern Portugal.
       </div>

     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:LGPK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/LGPK.jpg/220px-LGPK.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/LGPK.jpg/330px-LGPK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/LGPK.jpg/440px-LGPK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:LGPK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Oeiras,_Portugal" title="Oeiras, Portugal">Oeiras</a>, in 
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon Metropolitan Area</a>, houses many multinational companies operating in Portugal.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Portuguese currency is the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> (€), which replaced the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Escudo" title="Portuguese Escudo" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese Escudo</a>, and the country was one of the original member states of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>. Portugal's central bank is the <i><a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Portugal" title="Banco de Portugal">Banco de Portugal</a></i>, an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a>. Most industries, businesses and financial institutions are concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Metropolitan_Area_of_Porto" title="Greater Metropolitan Area of Porto" class="mw-redirect">Porto</a> metropolitan areas—the <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal_District" title="Setúbal District">Setúbal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aveiro_District" title="Aveiro District">Aveiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braga_District" title="Braga District">Braga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_District" title="Coimbra District">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leiria_District" title="Leiria District">Leiria</a> districts are the biggest economic centres outside these two main areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> According to World Travel Awards, Portugal is the Europe's Leading Golf Destination 2012 and 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> of 1974, which culminated in the end of one of Portugal's most notable <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">phases of economic expansion</a> (that started in the 1960s),<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> a significant change has occurred in the nation's annual economic growth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After the turmoil of the 1974 revolution and the <a href="/wiki/PREC" title="PREC" class="mw-redirect">PREC</a> period, Portugal tried to adapt to a changing <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">modern global economy</a>, a process that continues in 2013. Since the 1990s, Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Consumption_(economics)" title="Consumption (economics)">public consumption</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> model has been slowly changing to a system that is focused on exports, <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">private investment</a> and the development of the <a href="/wiki/High-tech" title="High-tech" class="mw-redirect">high-tech</a> sector. Consequently, business services have overtaken more traditional industries such as textiles, clothing, footwear and <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">cork</a> (Portugal is the world's leading cork producer),<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> wood products and beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-79">[78]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the second decade of the 21st century the Portuguese economy suffered its most severe recession since the 1970s resulting in the country having to be bailed out by the European Commission, European Central Bank and International Monetary Fund. The bailout, agreed to in 2011, required Portugal to enter into a range of austerity measures in exchange for funding support of €78 billion. In May 2014 the country exited the bailout but reaffirmed its commitment to maintaining its reformist momentum. At the time of exiting the bailout the economy had contracted by 0.7% in the first quarter of 2014, however unemployment, while still high had fallen to 15.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-PortugalBailoutEnds_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PortugalBailoutEnds-80">[79]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sectors">Sectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_sector">Primary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Primary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Portugal" title="Agriculture in Portugal">Agriculture in Portugal</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Portugal" title="Fishing in Portugal">Fishing in Portugal</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Portugal" title="Mining in Portugal">Mining in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Portugal" title="Agriculture in Portugal">Agriculture in Portugal</a> is based on small to medium-sized family-owned dispersed units. However, the sector also includes larger scale <a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">intensive farming</a> export-oriented <a href="/wiki/Agrobusiness" title="Agrobusiness" class="mw-redirect">agrobusinesses</a> backed by companies (like <a href="/wiki/Grupo_RAR" title="Grupo RAR">Grupo RAR</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Vitacress" title="Vitacress">Vitacress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovena" title="Sovena" class="mw-redirect">Sovena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lactogal" title="Lactogal">Lactogal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vale_da_Rosa" title="Vale da Rosa">Vale da Rosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Companhia_das_Lez%C3%ADrias" title="Companhia das Lezírias">Companhia das Lezírias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valouro" title="Valouro">Valouro</a>). The country produces a wide variety of crops and livestock products, including <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_vegetables" title="Green vegetables" class="mw-redirect">green vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn" title="Corn" class="mw-redirect">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oilseed" title="Oilseed" class="mw-redirect">oilseeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilberry" title="Bilberry">bilberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_grapes" title="Table grapes" class="mw-redirect">table grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edible_mushroom" title="Edible mushroom">edible mushrooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dairy_products" title="Dairy products" class="mw-redirect">dairy products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">Forestry</a> has also played an important economic role among the rural communities and industry (namely <a href="/wiki/Paper_industry" title="Paper industry" class="mw-redirect">paper industry</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/Portucel_Soporcel_Group" title="Portucel Soporcel Group" class="mw-redirect">Portucel Soporcel Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineered_wood" title="Engineered wood">engineered wood</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/Sonae_Ind%C3%BAstria" title="Sonae Indústria">Sonae Indústria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a> that includes several manufacturing plants in and around <a href="/wiki/Pa%C3%A7os_de_Ferreira" title="Paços de Ferreira">Paços de Ferreira</a>, the core of Portugal's major industrial operations of <a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">IKEA</a>). In 2001, the gross agricultural product accounted for 4 per cent of the national GDP.</p> 
     <p>Traditionally a sea-power, Portugal has had a strong tradition in <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Portugal" title="Fishing in Portugal">the Portuguese fishing sector</a> and is one of the countries with the highest fish consumption per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> The main landing sites in Portugal (including Azores and Madeira), according to total landings in weight by year, are the harbours of <a href="/wiki/Matosinhos" title="Matosinhos">Matosinhos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peniche,_Portugal" title="Peniche, Portugal">Peniche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olh%C3%A3o" title="Olhão">Olhão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesimbra" title="Sesimbra">Sesimbra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figueira_da_Foz" title="Figueira da Foz">Figueira da Foz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sines,_Portugal" title="Sines, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Sines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portim%C3%A3o" title="Portimão">Portimão</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>. Portuguese processed fish products are exported through several companies, under a number of different brands and registered trademarks, such as <a href="/wiki/Conservas_Ramirez" title="Conservas Ramirez">Ramirez</a> (the world’s oldest active canned fish producer), Bom Petisco, Nero, Combate, Comur, General, Líder, <a href="/wiki/Mann%C3%A1" title="Manná" class="mw-redirect">Manná</a>, Murtosa, Pescador, Pitéu, Tenório, Torreira and Vasco da Gama.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Portugal is a significant European <a href="/wiki/Minerals" title="Minerals" class="mw-redirect">minerals</a> producer and is ranked among Europe's leading <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> producers. The nation is also a notable producer of <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. However, the country lacks the potential to conduct <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">hydrocarbon exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>, a limitation that has hindered the development of Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Portugal" title="Mining in Portugal">mining</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a> sectors. Although the country has vast iron and coal reserves—mainly in the north—after the 1974 revolution and the consequent economic globalization, low competitiveness forced a decrease in the extraction activity for these minerals. The <a href="/wiki/Panasqueira" title="Panasqueira">Panasqueira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neves-Corvo_mine" title="Neves-Corvo mine">Neves-Corvo mines</a> are among the most recognised Portuguese mines that are still in operation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_sector">Secondary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Secondary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>Industry is diversified, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automotive</a> (<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Autoeuropa" title="Volkswagen Autoeuropa" class="mw-redirect">Volkswagen Autoeuropa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_Citroen" title="Peugeot Citroen" class="mw-redirect">Peugeot Citroen</a>), <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_industry" title="Aerospace industry" class="mw-redirect">aerospace</a> (<a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> and <a href="/wiki/OGMA" title="OGMA">OGMA</a>), <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry" title="Electronics industry">electronics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textiles</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood_pulp" title="Wood pulp" class="mw-redirect">wood pulp</a>. Volkswagen Group's <a href="/wiki/AutoEuropa" title="AutoEuropa">AutoEuropa</a> motor vehicle assembly plant in <a href="/wiki/Palmela" title="Palmela">Palmela</a> is among the largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> projects in Portugal. Modern non-traditional technology-based industries, such as <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, have been developed in several locations across the country. <a href="/wiki/Alverca" title="Alverca" class="mw-redirect">Alverca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Covilh%C3%A3" title="Covilhã">Covilhã</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vora" title="Évora">Évora</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ponte_de_Sor" title="Ponte de Sor">Ponte de Sor</a> are the main centres of the Portuguese aerospace industry, which is led by Brazil-based company Embraer and the Portuguese company OGMA. Following the turn of the 21st century, many major biotechnology and information technology industries have been founded, and are concentrated in the metropolitan areas of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Metropolitan_Area" title="Porto Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal" title="Aveiro, Portugal">Aveiro</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_sector">Tertiary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tertiary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>Travel and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">tourism</a> continue to be extremely important for Portugal, with visitor numbers forecast to increase significantly in the future.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, the increasing competition from Eastern European destinations continues to develop, with the presence of similar attractions that are often cheaper in countries such as Croatia. Consequently, it has been necessary for the country to focus upon its niche attractions, such as health, nature and rural tourism, to stay ahead of its competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The banking and insurance sectors performed well until the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">late-2000s financial crisis</a>, and this partly reflected a rapid deepening of the market in Portugal. While sensitive to various types of market and underwriting <a href="/wiki/Risk" title="Risk">risks</a>, it has been estimated that overall both the life and non-life sectors will be able to withstand a number of severe shocks, even though the impact on individual insurers varies widely.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State-owned_companies">State-owned companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: State-owned companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Major <a href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" title="Government-owned corporation" class="mw-redirect">State-owned companies</a> include <a href="/wiki/%C3%81guas_de_Portugal" title="Águas de Portugal">Águas de Portugal</a> (water), <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Geral_de_Dep%C3%B3sitos" title="Caixa Geral de Depósitos">Caixa Geral de Depósitos</a> (banking), <a href="/wiki/Comboios_de_Portugal" title="Comboios de Portugal">Comboios de Portugal</a> (railways), <a href="/wiki/Companhia_das_Lez%C3%ADrias" title="Companhia das Lezírias">Companhia das Lezírias</a> (agriculture) and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1dio_e_Televis%C3%A3o_de_Portugal" title="Rádio e Televisão de Portugal">RTP</a> (media). Some former state-owned entities are managed by state-run <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> <a href="/wiki/Parp%C3%BAblica" title="Parpública">Parpública</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholder</a> of several public and private companies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Among former State owned companies recently privatized are <a href="/wiki/CTT_Correios_de_Portugal,_S.A." title="CTT Correios de Portugal, S.A.">CTT</a> (postal service), <a href="/wiki/TAP_Portugal" title="TAP Portugal">TAP Portugal</a> (airline) and <a href="/wiki/ANA_Aeroportos_de_Portugal" title="ANA Aeroportos de Portugal">ANA</a> (airports).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Listed_companies">Listed companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Listed companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Companies listed on <a href="/wiki/Euronext_Lisbon" title="Euronext Lisbon">Euronext Lisbon</a> <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> like <a href="/wiki/Energias_de_Portugal" title="Energias de Portugal">EDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galp_Energia" title="Galp Energia">Galp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimo_Martins" title="Jerónimo Martins">Jerónimo Martins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mota-Engil" title="Mota-Engil">Mota-Engil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novabase" title="Novabase">Novabase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semapa" title="Semapa">Semapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portucel_Soporcel" title="Portucel Soporcel">Portucel Soporcel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Telecom" title="Portugal Telecom">Portugal Telecom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonae" title="Sonae">Sonae</a>, are among the largest corporations of Portugal by number of employees, <a href="/wiki/Net_income" title="Net income">net income</a> or international <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a>. The Euronext Lisbon is the major stock exchange of Portugal and is part of the <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a>, the first global stock exchange. The <a href="/wiki/PSI-20" title="PSI-20">PSI-20</a> is Portugal's most selective and widely known <a href="/wiki/Stock_index" title="Stock index" class="mw-redirect">stock index</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance">Performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Reserves.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/230px-Gold_Reserves.png" width="230" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/345px-Gold_Reserves.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/460px-Gold_Reserves.png 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="1640"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Reserves.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Portugal has the 13th highest 
        <a href="/wiki/Gold_reserves" title="Gold reserves" class="mw-redirect">gold reserves</a> in the world
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> for 2014-2015, published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, placed Portugal on the 36th position on the economic index. This represents a sharp increase from the 51st position where Portugal appeared in 2013-2014.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>'s quality of life index placed Portugal as the country with the 19th-best quality of life in the world for 2005, ahead of other economically and technologically advanced countries like France, Germany, the United Kingdom and South Korea, but 9 places behind its only neighbour, Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> This is despite the fact that Portugal remains one of the countries with the lowest per capita GDP in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-economia.publico.clix.pt_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economia.publico.clix.pt-87">[86]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The poor performance of the Portuguese economy was explored in April 2007 by <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>, which described Portugal as "a new <a href="/wiki/Sick_man_of_Europe" title="Sick man of Europe">sick man of Europe</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-sick_man_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sick_man-88">[87]</a></sup> From 2002 to 2007, the number of unemployed increased by 65% (270,500 unemployed citizens in 2002, 448,600 unemployed citizens in 2007).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> By early December 2009, the unemployment rate had reached 10.2%&nbsp;– a 23-year record high. In December 2009, ratings agency <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> lowered its long-term credit assessment of Portugal to "negative" from "stable," voicing pessimism on the country's structural weaknesses in the economy and weak competitiveness that would hamper growth and the capacity to strengthen its <a href="/wiki/Public_finances" title="Public finances" class="mw-redirect">public finances</a> and reduce <a href="/wiki/Public_debt" title="Public debt" class="mw-redirect">debt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> In July 2011, ratings agency <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" title="Moody's" class="mw-redirect">Moody's</a> downgraded its long-term credit assessment of Portugal after warning of deteriorating risk of default in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Corruption has become an issue of major political and economic significance for the country. Some cases are well known and were widely reported in the media, such as the affairs in several municipalities that involved local town hall officials, businesspersons, and a number of politicians with wider responsibilities and power.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> report places Portugal in 31st position for perceived corruption, just below Israel and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to a 2013 report from the <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a> quoted by the EU Observer Portugal is the most corrupt Country in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Over time, the Portuguese economy converged with EU levels, with the period from 1986 to the early 2000s of particular significance.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tcd.ie_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcd.ie-97">[96]</a></sup> According to Barry (2003), "what appears to have been crucial in the Portuguese case, relative to Spain at least, is the degree of labour-market flexibility that the economy exhibits.... Thus Portuguese convergence has been impressive, even though, consistent with its relatively low human-capital stock, the economy has specialised in low-tech production."<sup id="cite_ref-tcd.ie_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcd.ie-97">[96]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 6 April 2011, after his proposed "Plan for Stability and Growth IV" (PEC IV) was rejected by the Parliament, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_S%C3%B3crates" title="José Sócrates">José Sócrates</a> announced on national television that the country would request financial assistance from the IMF and the <a href="/wiki/European_Financial_Stability_Facility" title="European Financial Stability Facility">European Financial Stability Facility</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> had done previously. It was the third time that the Portuguese government had requested external financial aid from the IMF—the first occasion occurred in the late 1970s following the Carnation's Revolution. In October 2011, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investor_Services" title="Moody's Investor Services" class="mw-redirect">Moody's Investor Services</a> downgraded nine Portuguese banks due to financial weakness.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_sector">Public sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Public sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>In 2005, the number of public employees per thousand inhabitants in the Portuguese government (70.8) was above the European Union average (62.4 per thousand inhabitants). By EU and USA standards, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_legal_system" title="Portuguese legal system" class="mw-redirect">Portugal's justice system</a> was internationally known as being slow and inefficient, and by 2011 it was the second slowest in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> (after Italy); conversely, Portugal has one of the highest rates of <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">judges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prosecutor" title="Prosecutor">prosecutors</a>—over 30 per 100,000 people. The entire Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Public_service" title="Public service">public service</a> has been known for its mismanagement, useless redundancies, waste, excess of bureaucracy and a general lack of productivity in certain sectors, particularly in justice.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the first week of May 2013, Prime Minister Passos Coelho announced a significant government plan for the public sector, whereby 30,000 jobs will be cut and the number of weekly working hours will be increased from 35 to 40 hours. Coelho reaffirmed the announcement by explaining that austerity measures are necessary if Portugal seeks to avoid another monetary bailout grant from the European Commission, European Central Bank and International Monetary Fund—the overall plan intends to enact further cuts of €4.8 billion over a three-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-Marina_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marina-100">[99]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ongoing_policies.2C_reactions_and_consequences">Ongoing policies, reactions and consequences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ongoing policies, reactions and consequences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>Passos Coelho also announced that the retirement age will be increased from 65 to 66, announced cuts in the pensions, unemployment benefits, health, education and science expenses, abolished the English obligatory classes in Basic Education, but kept the pensions of the judges, diplomats untouched and didn't raise the retirement age of the military and police forces. He has, however, cut meaningfully the politicians salaries. These policies have led to social unrest and to confrontations between several institutions, namely between the Government and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court" title="Constitutional Court" class="mw-redirect">Constitutional Court</a>. Several individualities belonging to the parties that support the government have also raised their voices against the policies that have been taken in order to try to solve the financial crisis.</p> 
     <p>Since 2011, the Portuguese economy has already shrunk 4.5% and it's predicted that it will shrink more 2.3% in 2013 (totaling 6.7%). The Portuguese population has been shrinking since 2009 due to emigration caused by the economic crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-pordata.pt_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pordata.pt-101">[100]</a></sup> Between 2009 and 2012 the unemployed population rose from 473,000 to 769,000.<sup id="cite_ref-pordata.pt_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pordata.pt-101">[100]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the number of people in situation of poverty rose to 2.7 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Labour market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Portugal is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries" class="mw-redirect">developed</a> and a <a href="/wiki/High_income_countries" title="High income countries" class="mw-redirect">high income country</a>. However, its income per capita figure is still one of the lowest among the EU's member states. Portugal's GDP per capita in 2014 was 78% of the EU27 average - increasing from 76% in 2012, but still not achieving the 81% of 2009 and 2010 - making it the eleventh lowest in the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The average wage in Portugal is 910 € per month (net), excluding self-employed individuals<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>, which is regulated/ref by law, is €530 per month (paid 14 times per annum).</p> 
     <p>After years of high increase, the unemployment in Portugal has been in a continuous falling trend since the third quarter of 2014, decreasing from a peak of 17.7% achieved in the early 2013 to a rate of 11.9% in the second quarter of 2015. However, it is high still high compared with what was the normal average Portuguese unemployment rate in the past. In the second quarter of 2008 the unemployment rate was 7.3%,<sup id="cite_ref-unemployment_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unemployment-105">[104]</a></sup> but the rate immediately rose the following period. By December 2009, unemployment had surpassed the 10% mark nationwide in the wake of worldwide events, by 2010, the rate was around 11% and in 2011 it was above 12%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The first quarter of 2013 signified a new unemployment rate record for Portugal, as it reached 17.7%— up from 17% in the previous quarter — and the Government has predicted an 18.5% unemployment rate in 2014. However, in the third quarter of the same year, it has surprisingly declined to a rate of 15.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-Marina_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marina-100">[99]</a></sup> From then on, the unemployment downtrend continued, declining to 13.9% in the second semester of 2014 and to 11.9% in the second quarter of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">Tourism in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nazare_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Nazare_001.jpg/190px-Nazare_001.jpg" width="190" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Nazare_001.jpg/285px-Nazare_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Nazare_001.jpg/380px-Nazare_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nazare_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Nazar%C3%A9,_Portugal" title="Nazaré, Portugal">Nazaré</a>, worldwide known for its geological formation, idealizing the 
        <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a> practice. Nazaré is where the world's largest wave was ever surfed, in 2013, by the Hawaiian surfer 
        <a href="/wiki/Garrett_McNamara" title="Garrett McNamara">Garrett McNamara</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg/220px-Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg/330px-Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg/440px-Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2333"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sintra_Portugal_Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Pena-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Pena_Palace" title="Pena Palace" class="mw-redirect">Pena Palace</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Sintra_Municipality" title="Sintra Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Sintra</a>, a 
        <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> and an important tourist landmark.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal is among the 20 most visited countries in the world, receiving an average of 13 million foreign tourists each year.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Tourism is playing an increasingly important role in Portugal's economy, contributing to about 5% of its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Tourist hotspots in Portugal are Lisbon, Algarve, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, Porto and the city of <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>, also, between 4-5 million religious pilgrims visit <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A1tima,_Portugal" title="Fátima, Portugal">Fátima</a> each year, where apparitions of the Blessed Virgin Mary to three shepherd children reportedly took place in 1917. The <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_F%C3%A1tima" title="Sanctuary of Fátima">Sanctuary of Fátima</a> is one of the largest Roman Catholic shrines in the world. The Portuguese government continues to promote and develop new tourist destinations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro Valley</a>, the island of <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Island" title="Porto Santo Island">Porto Santo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>. Lisbon is the 16th European city which attracts the most tourists<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> (with seven million tourists occupying the city's hotels in 2006, a number that grew 11.8% compared to previous year).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Lisbon in recent years surpassed the Algarve as the leading tourist region in Portugal. Porto and Northern Portugal, especially the urban areas north of Douro River valley, was the tourist destination which grew most (11.9%) in 2006, surpassing Madeira (in 2010), as the third most visited destination.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Most tourists in Portugal are British-, French-, Spanish-, Dutch- or German-origin visitors, travel by <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low cost airliners</a>, and not only seek sun and beaches, but increasingly search for cultural, gastronomic, environmental or <a href="/wiki/Nautical_tourism" title="Nautical tourism">nautical</a> experiences (or travel for reasons of business).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>In 2014, Portugal was elected <i>The Best European Country</i> by the <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:858px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style=""> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of the Historic Centre of Porto, a UNESCO World Heritage Site. The city is known worldwide for being the centre for Port Wine."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg/850px-Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg" width="850" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg/1275px-Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg/1700px-Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5776" data-file-height="1002"></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002_edit2.jpg" title="File:Porto3flat-cc-contr-oliv1002 edit2.jpg"></a>
        </div> Panorama of the Historic Centre of 
        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, a 
        <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site" class="mw-redirect">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. The city is known worldwide for being the centre for 
        <a href="/wiki/Port_Wine" title="Port Wine" class="mw-redirect">Port Wine</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_regions">Tourist regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Tourist regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204"></a>
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help improve this section by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
