       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Aveiro_Canal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Aveiro_Canal.jpg/240px-Aveiro_Canal.jpg" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Aveiro_Canal.jpg/360px-Aveiro_Canal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Aveiro_Canal.jpg/480px-Aveiro_Canal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="3056"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Aveiro_Canal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Its historic background, cathedrals and canals, make 
        <a href="/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal" title="Aveiro, Portugal">Aveiro</a> scenic enough to be also known as the "Portuguese Venice".
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The main tourist regions can be broken-down into: the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Lisbon" title="Greater Lisbon" class="mw-redirect">Greater Lisbon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i><a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisboa</a></i></span>), the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Porto" title="Greater Porto" class="mw-redirect">Greater Porto</a> and Northern Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i><a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norte_Region,_Portugal" title="Norte Region, Portugal">Norte</a></i></span>), the Portuguese Islands (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Ilhas Portuguesas</i></span>: <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>. Other tourist regions include <i>Douro Sul</i>, <i>Templários</i>, <i>Dão-Lafões</i>, <i>Costa do Sol</i>, <i>Costa Azul</i>, <i>Planície Dourada</i>, that are unknown to many tourists or visitors.</p> 
     <p>Most of these regions are grouped in tourism reference areas, which continue to be in a state of reorganization and evolution, some based on the traditional regions of Portugal: the <i>Costa Verde</i> (<i>Green Coast</i>); <i>Costa da Prata</i> (<i>Silver Coast)</i>; <i>Costa de Lisboa</i> (<i>Lisbon Coast</i>); <i>Montanhas</i> (<i>Mountains</i>); <i>Planícies</i> (<i>Plains</i>); <i><a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a></i>; and the islands of the archipelagos of <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>.</p> 
     <p>The legend of the Rooster of Barcelos tells the story of a dead rooster's miraculous intervention in proving the innocence of a man who had been falsely accused and sentenced to death. The story is associated with the 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Calvary_(sculpture)" title="Calvary (sculpture)">calvary</a> that is part of the collection of the Archeological Museum located in Paço dos Condes, a gothic-style palace in <a href="/wiki/Barcelos,_Portugal" title="Barcelos, Portugal">Barcelos</a>, a city in the <a href="/wiki/Braga_District" title="Braga District">Braga District</a> of northwest Portugal. The <a href="/wiki/Rooster_of_Barcelos" title="Rooster of Barcelos">Rooster of Barcelos</a> is bought by many tourists as a <a href="/wiki/Souvenir" title="Souvenir">souvenir</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Portugal" title="Transport in Portugal">Transport in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214;_CS-TNJ@FNC;12.07.2011_607bc_(5940056994).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg/240px-TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg" width="240" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg/360px-TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg/480px-TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214%3B_CS-TNJ%40FNC%3B12.07.2011_607bc_%285940056994%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2459" data-file-height="1590"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TAP_Air_Portugal_Airbus_A320-214;_CS-TNJ@FNC;12.07.2011_607bc_(5940056994).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A plane of 
        <a href="/wiki/TAP_Portugal" title="TAP Portugal">TAP Portugal</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>By the early 1970s Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">fast economic growth</a> with increasing <a href="/wiki/Mass_consumption" title="Mass consumption" class="mw-redirect">consumption</a> and purchase of new automobiles set the priority for improvements in transportation. Again in the 1990s, after joining the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, the country built many new motorways. Today, the country has a 68,732&nbsp;km (42,708&nbsp;mi) road network, of which almost 3,000&nbsp;km (1,864&nbsp;mi) are part of system of 44 motorways. Opened in 1944, the first motorway (which linked Lisbon to the National Stadium) was an innovative project that made Portugal among one of the first countries in the world to establish a motorway (this roadway eventually became the Lisbon-Cascais highway, or A5). But, although a few other tracts were created (around 1960 and 1970), it was only after the beginning of the 1980s that large-scale motorway construction was implemented. In 1972, <a href="/wiki/BRISA_Auto-estradas_de_Portugal_S.A." title="BRISA Auto-estradas de Portugal S.A." class="mw-redirect">Brisa</a>, the highway concessionaire, was founded to handle the management of many of the regions motorways. On many highways, toll needs to be paid, see <a href="/wiki/Via_Verde" title="Via Verde">Via Verde</a>. <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_bridge" title="Vasco da Gama bridge" class="mw-redirect">Vasco da Gama bridge</a> is the longest bridge in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Continental_Portugal" title="Continental Portugal">Continental Portugal</a>'s 89,015&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (34,369&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) territory is serviced by four international airports located near the principal cities of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">Faro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beja_(Portugal)" title="Beja (Portugal)" class="mw-redirect">Beja</a>. Lisbon's geographical position makes it a stopover for many foreign airlines at several airports within the country. The primary <a href="/wiki/Flag-carrier" title="Flag-carrier" class="mw-redirect">flag-carrier</a> is <a href="/wiki/TAP_Portugal" title="TAP Portugal">TAP Portugal</a>, although many other domestic airlines provide services within and without the country. The government decided to build a new airport outside Lisbon, in <a href="/wiki/Alcochete" title="Alcochete">Alcochete</a>, to replace <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Portela_Airport" title="Lisbon Portela Airport">Lisbon Portela Airport</a>, though this plan has been stalled due to the austerity. Currently, the most important airports are in <a href="/wiki/Portela_Airport" title="Portela Airport" class="mw-redirect">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_S%C3%A1_Carneiro_Airport" title="Francisco Sá Carneiro Airport" class="mw-redirect">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faro_Airport" title="Faro Airport">Faro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Airport" title="Madeira Airport">Funchal</a> (Madeira), and <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Paulo_II_Airport" title="João Paulo II Airport">Ponta Delgada</a> (Azores), managed by the national airport authority group <a href="/wiki/ANA_%E2%80%93_Aeroportos_de_Portugal" title="ANA – Aeroportos de Portugal" class="mw-redirect">ANA&nbsp;– Aeroportos de Portugal</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg/260px-Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg" width="260" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg/390px-Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg/520px-Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="545"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Metro-Almada-Portugal3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">LRV</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Almada_Municipality" title="Almada Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Almada</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A national railway system that extends throughout the country and into Spain, is supported and administered by <a href="/wiki/Comboios_de_Portugal" title="Comboios de Portugal">Comboios de Portugal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">Rail transport</a> of passengers and goods is derived using the 2,791&nbsp;km (1,734&nbsp;mi) of railway lines currently in service, of which 1,430&nbsp;km (889&nbsp;mi) are electrified and about 900&nbsp;km (559&nbsp;mi) allow train speeds greater than 120&nbsp;km/h (75&nbsp;mph). The railway network is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Rede_Ferrovi%C3%A1ria_Nacional" title="Rede Ferroviária Nacional">REFER</a> while the transport of passengers and goods are the responsibility of <a href="/wiki/Comboios_de_Portugal" title="Comboios de Portugal">Comboios de Portugal</a> (CP), both public companies. In 2006 the CP carried 133&nbsp;million passengers and 9,750,000&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a> (9,600,000 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a>; 10,700,000 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a>) of goods.</p> 
     <p>The major seaports are located in <a href="/wiki/Sines,_Portugal" title="Sines, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Sines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leix%C3%B5es" title="Leixões">Leixões</a>, <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">Setúbal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal" title="Aveiro, Portugal">Aveiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figueira_da_Foz" title="Figueira da Foz">Figueira da Foz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Faro,_Portugal" title="Faro, Portugal">Faro</a>.</p> 
     <p>The two largest metropolitan areas have subway systems: <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metro" title="Lisbon Metro">Lisbon Metro</a> and <i>Metro Sul do Tejo</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon Metropolitan Area</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Metro" title="Porto Metro">Porto Metro</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Porto_Metropolitan_Area" title="Porto Metropolitan Area" class="mw-redirect">Porto Metropolitan Area</a>, each with more than 35&nbsp;km (22&nbsp;mi) of lines. In Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Lisbon" title="Trams in Lisbon">Lisbon tram services</a> have been supplied by the <i>Companhia de Carris de Ferro de Lisboa</i> (<a href="/wiki/Carris" title="Carris">Carris</a>), for over a century. In <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Porto" title="Trams in Porto">a tram network</a>, of which only a tourist line on the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> remain, began construction on 12 September 1895 (a first for the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>). All major cities and towns have their own local urban transport network, as well as taxi services.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Portugal" title="Science and technology in Portugal">Science and technology in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nanotecnologia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Nanotecnologia.jpg/220px-Nanotecnologia.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Nanotecnologia.jpg/330px-Nanotecnologia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Nanotecnologia.jpg/440px-Nanotecnologia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3616" data-file-height="1856"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nanotecnologia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/International_Iberian_Nanotechnology_Laboratory" title="International Iberian Nanotechnology Laboratory">International Iberian Nanotechnology Laboratory</a>, in 
        <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Scientific and technological research activities in Portugal are mainly conducted within a network of <a href="/wiki/R%26D" title="R&amp;D" class="mw-redirect">R&amp;D</a> units belonging to <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Portugal" title="List of universities in Portugal" class="mw-redirect">public universities</a> and state-managed autonomous research institutions like the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Engenharia,_Tecnologia_e_Inova%C3%A7%C3%A3o" title="Instituto Nacional de Engenharia, Tecnologia e Inovação">INETI&nbsp;– Instituto Nacional de Engenharia, Tecnologia e Inovação</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_dos_Recursos_Biol%C3%B3gicos" title="Instituto Nacional dos Recursos Biológicos">INRB&nbsp;– Instituto Nacional dos Recursos Biológicos</a>. The funding and management of this research system is mainly conducted under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Science,_Technology_and_Higher_Education" title="Ministry of Science, Technology and Higher Education">Ministry of Science, Technology and Higher Education</a> (MCTES) itself and the MCTES's <a href="/wiki/Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_para_a_Ci%C3%AAncia_e_Tecnologia" title="Fundação para a Ciência e Tecnologia">Fundação para a Ciência e Tecnologia</a> (FCT). The largest R&amp;D units of the public universities by volume of research grants and peer-reviewed publications, include <a href="/wiki/Biosciences" title="Biosciences" class="mw-redirect">biosciences</a> research institutions like the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Medicina_Molecular" title="Instituto de Medicina Molecular">Instituto de Medicina Molecular</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Neuroscience_and_Cell_Biology" title="Centre for Neuroscience and Cell Biology">Centre for Neuroscience and Cell Biology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/IPATIMUP" title="IPATIMUP" class="mw-redirect">IPATIMUP</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Biologia_Molecular_e_Celular" title="Instituto de Biologia Molecular e Celular">Instituto de Biologia Molecular e Celular</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abel_Salazar_Biomedical_Sciences_Institute" title="Abel Salazar Biomedical Sciences Institute">Abel Salazar Biomedical Sciences Institute</a>.</p> 
     <p>Among the largest non-state-run research institutions in Portugal are the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Gulbenkian_de_Ci%C3%AAncia" title="Instituto Gulbenkian de Ciência">Instituto Gulbenkian de Ciência</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Champalimaud_Foundation" title="Champalimaud Foundation">Champalimaud Foundation</a>, a neuroscience and oncology research centre, which in addition awards every year one of the highest monetary prizes of any science prize in the world. A number of both national and multinational high-tech and industrial companies, are also responsible for research and development projects. One of the oldest learned societies of Portugal is the <a href="/wiki/Sciences_Academy_of_Lisbon" title="Sciences Academy of Lisbon" class="mw-redirect">Sciences Academy of Lisbon</a>, founded in 1779.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Moniz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Moniz.jpg/170px-Moniz.jpg" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Moniz.jpg/255px-Moniz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Moniz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="396"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Moniz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Egas_Moniz" title="António Egas Moniz">António Egas Moniz</a> was a Portuguese 
        <a href="/wiki/Neurologist" title="Neurologist" class="mw-redirect">neurologist</a> awarded with the 
        <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" title="Iberian peninsula" class="mw-redirect">Iberian</a> bilateral state-supported research efforts include the <a href="/wiki/International_Iberian_Nanotechnology_Laboratory" title="International Iberian Nanotechnology Laboratory">International Iberian Nanotechnology Laboratory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ibercivis" title="Ibercivis">Ibercivis</a> <a href="/wiki/Distributed_computing" title="Distributed computing">distributed computing</a> platform, which are joint research programmes of both Portugal and Spain. Portugal is a member of several pan-European scientific organizations. These include the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA), the <a href="/wiki/European_Laboratory_for_Particle_Physics" title="European Laboratory for Particle Physics" class="mw-redirect">European Laboratory for Particle Physics</a> (CERN), <a href="/wiki/ITER" title="ITER">ITER</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Southern_Observatory" title="European Southern Observatory">European Southern Observatory</a> (ESO).</p> 
     <p>Portugal has the largest <a href="/wiki/Aquarium" title="Aquarium">aquarium</a> in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Oceanarium" title="Lisbon Oceanarium">Lisbon Oceanarium</a>, and the Portuguese have several other notable organizations focused on science-related exhibits and divulgation, like the state agency <i>Ciência Viva</i>, a programme of the Portuguese Ministry of Science and Technology to the promotion of a scientific and technological culture among the Portuguese population,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Science_Museum_of_the_University_of_Coimbra" title="Science Museum of the University of Coimbra">Science Museum of the University of Coimbra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_natural_history_museums#Portugal" title="List of natural history museums">National Museum of Natural History</a> at the University of Lisbon, and the <a href="/wiki/Visionarium_(Portugal)" title="Visionarium (Portugal)">Visionarium</a>.</p> 
     <p>With the emergence and growth of several <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">science parks</a> throughout the world that helped create many thousands of scientific, technological and knowledge-based businesses, Portugal started to develop several<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> science parks across the country. These include the <a href="/wiki/Taguspark" title="Taguspark">Taguspark</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Oeiras_Municipality,_Portugal" title="Oeiras Municipality, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Oeiras</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_iParque" title="Coimbra iParque">Coimbra iParque</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Biocant" title="Biocant">biocant</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Cantanhede_Municipality" title="Cantanhede Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Cantanhede</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Tecnopolo" title="Madeira Tecnopolo">Madeira Tecnopolo</a><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> (in <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sines_Tecnopolo" title="Sines Tecnopolo">Sines Tecnopolo</a><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> (in <a href="/wiki/Sines,_Portugal" title="Sines, Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Sines</a>), Tecmaia<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> (in <a href="/wiki/Maia_Municipality" title="Maia Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Maia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Parkurbis" title="Parkurbis">Parkurbis</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> (in <a href="/wiki/Covilh%C3%A3" title="Covilhã">Covilhã</a>). Companies locate in the Portuguese science parks to take advantage of a variety of services ranging from financial and legal advice through to marketing and technological support.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Egas_Moniz" title="Egas Moniz" class="mw-redirect">Egas Moniz</a>, a Portuguese physician who developed the <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_angiography" title="Cerebral angiography">cerebral angiography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leucotomy" title="Leucotomy" class="mw-redirect">leucotomy</a>, received in 1949 the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a>&nbsp;– he is the first Portuguese recipient of a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> and the only in the sciences.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Innovation_Scoreboard" title="European Innovation Scoreboard">European Innovation Scoreboard</a> 2011, placed Portugal-based innovation in the 15th position, with an impressive increase in innovation expenditure and output.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Portugal" title="Energy in Portugal">Energy in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg/220px-Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg/330px-Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg/440px-Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pain%C3%A9is_Solares-Lagos.2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_panels" title="Solar panels" class="mw-redirect">Solar panels</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Lagos,_Portugal" title="Lagos, Portugal">Lagos</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal has considerable resources of wind and river power, the two most cost-effective renewable sources. Since the turn of the 21st century, there has been a trend towards the development of a renewable resource industry and reduction of both consumption and use of fossil fuel resources. In 2006, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar power</a> plant at that date, the <a href="/wiki/Moura_Photovoltaic_Power_Station" title="Moura Photovoltaic Power Station">Moura Photovoltaic Power Station</a>, began operating near <a href="/wiki/Moura,_Portugal" title="Moura, Portugal">Moura</a>, in the south, while the world's first commercial <a href="/wiki/Wave_power" title="Wave power">wave power</a> farm, the <a href="/wiki/Agu%C3%A7adoura_Wave_Farm" title="Aguçadoura Wave Farm">Aguçadoura Wave Farm</a>, opened in the <a href="/wiki/Norte_Region,_Portugal" title="Norte Region, Portugal">Norte region</a> (2008). By the end of 2006, 66% of the country's electrical production was from coal and fuel power plants, while 29% were derived from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric" title="Hydroelectric" class="mw-redirect">hydroelectric</a> dams, and 6% by <a href="/wiki/Wind_energy" title="Wind energy" class="mw-redirect">wind energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2008, renewable energy resources were producing 43% of the nation's consumption of electricity, even as hydroelectric production decreased with severe droughts.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> As of June 2010, electricity exports had outnumbered imports. In the period between January and May 2010, 70% of the national production of energy came from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Portugal’s national energy transmission company, <a href="/wiki/Redes_Energ%C3%A9ticas_Nacionais" title="Redes Energéticas Nacionais">Redes Energéticas Nacionais</a> (REN), uses sophisticated modeling to predict weather, especially wind patterns, and computer programs to calculate energy from the various renewable-energy plants. Before the solar/wind revolution, Portugal had generated electricity from hydropower plants on its rivers for decades. New programs combine wind and water: wind-driven turbines pump water uphill at night, the most blustery period; then the water flows downhill by day, generating electricity, when consumer demand is highest. Portugal’s distribution system is also now a two-way street. Instead of just delivering electricity, it draws electricity from even the smallest generators, like rooftop solar panels. The government aggressively encouraged such contributions by setting a premium price for those who buy rooftop-generated solar electricity.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Alqueva_dam.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alqueva_dam.JPG/220px-Alqueva_dam.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alqueva_dam.JPG/330px-Alqueva_dam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Alqueva_dam.JPG/440px-Alqueva_dam.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Alqueva_dam.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Alqueva_Dam" title="Alqueva Dam">Alqueva Dam</a> created the largest artificial lake in all of 
        <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Portugal" title="Water supply and sanitation in Portugal">Water supply and sanitation in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Water supply and sanitation services in Portugal have seen important advances in access to services, technologies used and service quality over the past decades (1980s–1990s), partially achieved thanks to important funds from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Nevertheless, sanitation still remains relatively low in mountain rural areas and some people have their own sources of water controlled by municipalities.</p> 
     <p>During the 1990s Portugal has put in place a modern institutional framework for the sector, which includes a national regulatory agency (ERSAR - The Water and Waste Services Regulation Authority) and multi-municipal water and sanitation companies.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Portugal" title="Demographics of Portugal">Demographics of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg/300px-Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg" width="300" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg/450px-Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg/600px-Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1293"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_31.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A view of 
        <a href="/wiki/Parque_das_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es" title="Parque das Nações">Parque das Nações</a>, in 
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, Portugal's capital and largest city with an 
        <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> with 2.8 million inhabitants.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Statistics Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>INE - <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estat%C3%ADstica" title="Instituto Nacional de Estatística">Instituto Nacional de Estatística</a></i></span>) estimates that, according to the 2011 census, the population was 10,562,178 (of which 52% was female, 48% was male). This population has been relatively homogeneous for most of its history: a single religion (Catholicism) and a single language have contributed to this ethnic and national unity, namely after the expulsion of the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> A considerable number of Moors and Jews, nevertheless, stayed in Portugal, under the condition that they converted to Catholicism, and afterwards they were known as <i>Mouriscos</i> (former Muslims) and <i>Cristãos Novos</i> (New Christians or former Jews) some of whom may have continued to observe rabbinic Judaism in secret, as in the case of the secret <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Belmonte" title="History of the Jews in Belmonte">Jews of Belmonte</a>, who now observe the Jewish faith openly. After 1772 the distinction between Old and New Christians was abolished by decree. Some famous Portuguese New Christians were the mathematician <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Nunes" title="Pedro Nunes">Pedro Nunes</a> and the physician and naturalist <a href="/wiki/Garcia_de_Orta" title="Garcia de Orta">Garcia de Orta</a>.</p> 
     <p>Native Portuguese are an <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian</a> ethnic group, whose ancestry is very similar to other <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern</a> Europeans and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_people" title="Mediterranean people" class="mw-redirect">Mediterranean peoples</a>, in particular Spaniards, followed by some regional French and Italians with whom they share a common ancestry, history and cultural proximity.</p> 
     <p>The most important demographic influence in the modern Portuguese seems to be the oldest one; current interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Y-chromosome" title="Y-chromosome" class="mw-redirect">Y-chromosome</a> and <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" title="MtDNA" class="mw-redirect">mtDNA</a> data suggests that the Portuguese have their origin in <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> peoples that began arriving to the European continent around 45,000 years ago. All subsequent migrations did leave an impact, genetically and culturally, but the main population source of the Portuguese is still Paleolithic. Genetic studies show Portuguese populations not to be significantly different from other European populations.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The total fertility rate (TFR) as of 2013 was estimated at 1.51 children born/woman, which is below the replacement rate of 2.1.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> In 2014, 49.3% of births were to unmarried women.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> Like most Western countries, Portugal has to deal with low fertility levels: the country has experienced a <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility_rate" title="Sub-replacement fertility rate" class="mw-redirect">sub-replacement fertility rate</a> since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The structure of Portuguese society is characterized by an increasing inequality which at present (2015) places the country in the lowest third of the Social Justice Index for the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_areas">Metropolitan areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Metropolitan areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_of_Portugal" title="Metropolitan areas of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Metropolitan areas of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png/250px-Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png" width="250" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png/375px-Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png/500px-Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="605"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Densidade_populacional_por_concelho_-_INE_2001.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A map of Portugal showing the population density (no. of inhabitants / km 
        <sup>2</sup>) by municipality.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are two Greater Metropolitan Areas (<a href="/wiki/Grande_%C3%81rea_Metropolitana" title="Grande Área Metropolitana" class="mw-redirect">GAMs</a>): <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rea_Metropolitana_de_Lisboa" title="Área Metropolitana de Lisboa" class="mw-redirect">Lisbon</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rea_Metropolitana_do_Porto" title="Área Metropolitana do Porto" class="mw-redirect">Porto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>

      </caption>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Portugal" title="Immigration to Portugal">Immigration to Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">colonial history</a> has long since been a cornerstone of its national identity, as has its geographic position at the south-western corner of Europe, looking out into the Atlantic Ocean. It was one of the last western colonial European powers to give up its overseas territories (among them <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa" class="mw-redirect">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_East_Africa" title="Portuguese East Africa" class="mw-redirect">Mozambique</a> in 1975), turning over the administration of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> to the People's Republic of China at the end of 1999. Consequently, it has both influenced and been influenced by cultures from former colonies or dependencies, resulting in immigration from these former territories for both economic and/or personal reasons. Portugal, long a country of emigration (the vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" title="Portuguese Brazilian" class="mw-redirect">Brazilians</a> have Portuguese ancestry),<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-132">[131]</a></sup> has now become a country of net immigration,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> and not just from the last <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Indian</a> (Portuguese until 1961), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">African</a> (Portuguese until 1975), and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Far East Asian</a> (Portuguese until 1999) overseas territories. An estimated 800,000 Portuguese returned to Portugal as the country's African possessions gained independence in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-132">[131]</a></sup> By 2007, Portugal had 10,617,575 inhabitants of whom about 332,137 were legal <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Portugal" title="Immigration to Portugal">immigrants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ine.pt_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine.pt-134">[133]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since the 1990s, along with a boom in <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">construction</a>, several new waves of <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilians" title="Brazilians">Brazilian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">people from the former Portuguese colonies in Africa</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Africans" title="Africans" class="mw-redirect">Africans</a> have settled in the country. <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovar_diaspora" title="Kosovar diaspora" class="mw-redirect">Kosovar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> have also chosen Portugal as destination. Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a> population, estimated at about 40,000.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition, a number of <a href="/wiki/EU_citizen" title="EU citizen" class="mw-redirect">EU citizens</a>, mostly from the United Kingdom, other northern European or <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Nordic</a> countries, have become permanent residents in the country (with the British community being mostly composed of retired pensioners and choosing to live in the Algarve and Madeira).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Portugal" title="Religion in Portugal">Religion in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">

       <tbody>
