     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_shield.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Portuguese_shield.svg/150px-Portuguese_shield.svg.png" width="150" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Portuguese_shield.svg/225px-Portuguese_shield.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Portuguese_shield.svg/300px-Portuguese_shield.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="597"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_shield.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> On the Portuguese Arms, the white dots inside the blue shields represent the 
        <a href="/wiki/Five_Holy_Wounds" title="Five Holy Wounds">Five Holy Wounds of Jesus Christ</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>According to the 2011 Census, 81.0% of the Portuguese population are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic</a>. The country has small Protestant, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">Latter-day Saint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Portugal" title="Islam in Portugal">Muslim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Portugal" title="Hinduism in Portugal">Hindu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baha%27i" title="Baha'i" class="mw-redirect">Baha'i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">Spiritist</a> communities. Influences from <a href="/wiki/African_Traditional_Religion" title="African Traditional Religion" class="mw-redirect">African Traditional Religion</a> and Chinese Traditional Religion are also felt among many people, particularly in fields related with Traditional Chinese Medicine and African Witch Doctors. Some 6.8% of the population declared themselves to be non-religious, and 8.3% did not give any answer about their religion.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, a study conducted by the Catholic University revealed 79.5% of the Portuguese considered themselves Catholics, and that 18% <a href="/wiki/Church_attendance" title="Church attendance">attended Mass</a> regularly. These figures represent a drop from 86.9% of Catholics in 2001, while during the same period the number of people stating that they had no religion rose from 8.2% to 14.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many Portuguese holidays, festivals and traditions have a Christian origin or connotation. Although relations between the Portuguese state and the Roman Catholic Church were generally amiable and stable since the earliest years of the Portuguese nation, their relative power fluctuated. In the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1279-1415)" title="History of Portugal (1279-1415)" class="mw-redirect">13th and 14th centuries</a>, the church enjoyed both riches and power stemming from its role in the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">reconquest</a>, its close identification with early Portuguese nationalism and the foundation of the Portuguese educational system, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">first university</a>. The growth of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese overseas empire</a> made its <a href="/wiki/Mission_(Christian)" title="Mission (Christian)" class="mw-redirect">missionaries</a> important agents of <a href="/wiki/Colonisation" title="Colonisation" class="mw-redirect">colonization</a>, with important roles in the <a href="/wiki/Teaching" title="Teaching" class="mw-redirect">education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelization" title="Evangelization" class="mw-redirect">evangelization</a> of people from all the inhabited continents. The growth of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1820" title="Liberal Revolution of 1820">liberal</a> and nascent <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republican</a> movements during the eras leading to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/First_Portuguese_Republic" title="First Portuguese Republic">First Portuguese Republic</a> (1910–26) changed the role and importance of organized religion.</p> 
     <p>Portugal is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>: <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">church and state were formally separated</a> during the Portuguese First Republic, and later reiterated in the 1976 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitution" title="Portuguese Constitution" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese Constitution</a>. Other than the Constitution, the two most important documents relating to <a href="/wiki/Religious_freedom" title="Religious freedom" class="mw-redirect">religious freedom</a> in Portugal are: the 1940 Concordata (later amended in 1971) between Portugal and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, and the 2001 Religious Freedom Act.</p> 
     <p>On the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Portugal" title="Flag of Portugal">Flag of Portugal</a>, the Portuguese Arm rests over the <a href="/wiki/Armillary_sphere" title="Armillary sphere">armillary sphere</a>. Except during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso I</a>, it is present in every single historical flag, in one form or another. It is the prime Portuguese symbol as well as one of the oldest, with the first elements of today's shield appearing during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Sancho_I_of_Portugal" title="Sancho I of Portugal">Sancho I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sancho1185_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sancho1185-140">[139]</a></sup> The evolution of the Portuguese flag is inherently associated with the evolution of the shield.</p> 
     <p>Within the white inescutcheon, the five <i>quinas</i> (small blue shields) with their five white <a href="/wiki/Bezant" title="Bezant">bezants</a> representing the <a href="/wiki/Five_wounds_of_Christ" title="Five wounds of Christ" class="mw-redirect">five wounds of Christ</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Cinco Chagas</i></span>) when crucified and are popularly associated with the "Miracle of Ourique".<sup id="cite_ref-criarmundos_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-criarmundos-141">[140]</a></sup> The story associated with this miracle tells that before the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a> (25 July 1139), an old hermit appeared before Count Afonso Henriques (future Afonso I) as a divine messenger. He foretold Afonso's victory and assured him that God was watching over him and his peers. The messenger advised him to walk away from his camp, alone, if he heard a nearby chapel bell tolling, in the following night. In doing so, he witnessed an apparition of Jesus on the cross. Ecstatic, Afonso heard Jesus promising victories for the coming battles, as well as God's wish to act through Afonso, and his descendants, in order to create an empire which would carry His name to unknown lands, thus choosing the Portuguese to perform great tasks.<sup id="cite_ref-miracle_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miracle-142">[141]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Portugal" title="Languages of Portugal">Languages of Portugal</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/220px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/330px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/440px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="880"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Sign in 
        <a href="/wiki/Miranda_do_Douro" title="Miranda do Douro">Miranda do Douro</a>, in 
        <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese</a> (above) and Portuguese (below).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Macau_street_sign.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/220px-Macau_street_sign.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/330px-Macau_street_sign.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_street_sign.JPG/440px-Macau_street_sign.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Macau_street_sign.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> remains an official language in 
        <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> after the handover to 
        <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">China</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portuguese is the official language of Portugal. Portuguese is a <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language" class="mw-redirect">Romance language</a> that originated in what is now <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" title="Northern Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Northern Portugal</a>, originating from <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>, which was the common language of the Galician and Portuguese people until the independence of Portugal. Particularly in the North of Portugal, there are still many similarities between the Galician culture and the Portuguese culture. Galicia is a consultative observer of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>. According to the Ethnologue of Languages, Portuguese and Spanish have a lexical similarity of 89% - educated speakers of each language can communicate easily with one another.</p> 
     <p>The Portuguese language is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language" class="mw-redirect">Latin</a> spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">romanized</a> <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula</a> around 2000 years ago—particularly the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tartessians" title="Tartessians" class="mw-redirect">Tartessians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>. In the 15th and 16th centuries, the language spread worldwide as Portugal established a colonial and commercial empire between 1415 and 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> Portuguese is now spoken as a native language in five different continents, with Brazil accounting for the largest number of native Portuguese speakers of any country (200 million speakers in 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2013 the Portuguese language is the official language spoken in Brazil, Angola, Mozambique, Cape Verde, São Tomé and Príncipe, Guinea-Bissau, Equatorial Guinea, and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>. These countries, plus <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> Special Administrative Region (People's Republic of China) where Portuguese is co-official with Cantonese, make up the <a href="/wiki/Lusosphere" title="Lusosphere" class="mw-redirect">Lusosphere</a>, a term derived from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>", which currently matches the Portuguese territory south of the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> river.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese</a> is also recognized as a co-official regional language in some municipalities of North-Eastern Portugal. An estimate of between 6,000 and 7,000 Mirandese speakers has been documented for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <a href="/wiki/EF_English_Proficiency_Index" title="EF English Proficiency Index">International English Proficiency Index</a>, Portugal has a high proficiency level in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, proficiency higher than in countries like <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> or <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Portugal" title="Education in Portugal">Education in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Coimbra_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/220px-Coimbra_University.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/330px-Coimbra_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/440px-Coimbra_University.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Coimbra_University.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Courtyard at the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">University of Coimbra</a>. Built in 1290, it is Portugal's oldest university and one of the oldest in Europe
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The educational system is divided into preschool (for those under age 6), basic education (9 years, in three stages, compulsory), secondary education (3 years, compulsory since 2010), and higher education (subdivided in university and <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_(Portugal)" title="Polytechnic (Portugal)">polytechnic</a> education).</p> 
     <p>The total adult literacy rate is 99 percent. Portuguese primary school enrollments are close to 100 percent. According to the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD" class="mw-redirect">OECD</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> (PISA) 2009, the average Portuguese 15-year-old student, when rated in terms of reading literacy, mathematics and science knowledge, is placed at the same level as those students from the United States, Sweden, Germany, Ireland, France, Denmark, United Kingdom, Hungary and <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a>, with 489 points (493 is the average).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Over 35% of college-age citizens (20 years old) attend one of Portugal's higher education institutions<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> (compared with 50% in the United States and 35% in the OECD countries). In addition to being a destination for <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">international students</a>, Portugal is also among the top places of origin for international students. All higher education students, both domestic and international, totaled 380,937 in 2005.</p> 
     <p>Portuguese universities have existed since 1290. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">oldest Portuguese university</a> was first established in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> before moving to <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>. Historically, within the scope of the Portuguese Empire, the Portuguese founded the oldest engineering school of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> (the <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Academia_de_Artilharia,_Fortifica%C3%A7%C3%A3o_e_Desenho" title="Real Academia de Artilharia, Fortificação e Desenho" class="mw-redirect">Real Academia de Artilharia, Fortificação e Desenho</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>) in 1792, as well as the oldest medical college in Asia (the <i><a href="/wiki/Escola_M%C3%A9dico-Cir%C3%BArgica_de_Goa" title="Escola Médico-Cirúrgica de Goa" class="mw-redirect">Escola Médico-Cirúrgica</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>) in 1842. The largest university in Portugal is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lisbon" title="University of Lisbon">University of Lisbon</a>.</p> 
     <p>Universities are usually organized into <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">faculties</a>. Institutes and schools are also common designations for autonomous subdivisions of <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Portugal" title="List of colleges and universities in Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese higher education institutions</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" title="Bologna process" class="mw-redirect">Bologna process</a> has been adopted, since 2006, by Portuguese universities and poly-technical institutes. Higher education in state-run educational establishments is provided on a competitive basis, a system of <i><a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus" title="Numerus clausus">numerus clausus</a></i> is enforced through a national database on student admissions. However, every higher education institution offers also a number of additional vacant places through other extraordinary admission processes for sportsmen, mature applicants (over 23 years old), <a href="/wiki/International_students" title="International students" class="mw-redirect">international students</a>, foreign students from the <a href="/wiki/Lusosphere" title="Lusosphere" class="mw-redirect">Lusosphere</a>, degree owners from other institutions, students from other institutions (<a href="/wiki/Transfer_admissions_in_the_United_States" title="Transfer admissions in the United States">academic transfer</a>), former students (readmission), and course change, which are subject to specific standards and regulations set by each institution or course department.</p> 
     <p>Most student costs are supported with public money. However, with the increasing tuition fees a student has to pay to attend a Portuguese state-run higher education institution and the attraction of new types of students (many as part-time students or in evening classes) like employees, businessmen, parents, and pensioners, many departments make a substantial profit from every additional student enrolled in courses, with benefits for the college or university's gross tuition revenue and without loss of educational quality (teacher per student, computer per student, classroom size per student, etc.).</p> 
     <p>Portugal has entered into <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_Portugal#International_partnership_agreements" title="Higher education in Portugal">cooperation agreements with the Massachusetts Institute of Technology and other US institutions</a> to further develop and increase the effectiveness of Portuguese higher education and research.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Portugal" title="Health in Portugal">Health in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hoptial_Viseu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hoptial_Viseu.jpg/240px-Hoptial_Viseu.jpg" width="240" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hoptial_Viseu.jpg/360px-Hoptial_Viseu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Hoptial_Viseu.jpg/480px-Hoptial_Viseu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hoptial_Viseu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The Hospital of São Teotónio, in 
        <a href="/wiki/Viseu" title="Viseu">Viseu</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:245px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/243px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg" width="243" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/365px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/486px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The Hospital of Santa Maria, 
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>,
        <br> the largest hospital in the country
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>According to the latest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a>, the average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in 2015 was 81.0 years.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Portugal ranks 12th in the best public health systems in the world, ahead of high developed countries like the United Kingdom, Germany or Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Portuguese health system is characterized by three coexisting systems: the National Health Service (<i>Serviço Nacional de Saúde'</i>, SNS), special social health insurance schemes for certain professions (health subsystems) and voluntary private health insurance. The SNS provides universal coverage. In addition, about 25% of the population is covered by the health subsystems, 10% by private insurance schemes and another 7% by mutual funds.</p> 
     <p>The Ministry of Health is responsible for developing health policy as well as managing the SNS. Five regional health administrations are in charge of implementing the national health policy objectives, developing guidelines and protocols and supervising health care delivery. Decentralization efforts have aimed at shifting financial and management responsibility to the regional level. In practice, however, the autonomy of regional health administrations over budget setting and spending has been limited to primary care.</p> 
     <p>The SNS is predominantly funded through general taxation. Employer (including the state) and employee contributions represent the main funding sources of the health subsystems. In addition, direct payments by the patient and voluntary health insurance premiums account for a large proportion of funding.</p> 
     <p>Similar to the other Eur-A countries, most Portuguese die from <a href="/wiki/Noncommunicable_diseases" title="Noncommunicable diseases" class="mw-redirect">noncommunicable diseases</a>. Mortality from <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_diseases" title="Cardiovascular diseases" class="mw-redirect">cardiovascular diseases</a> (CVD) is higher than in the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>, but its two main components, ischaemic heart disease and cerebrovascular disease, display inverse trends compared with the Eur-A, with <a href="/wiki/Cerebrovascular_disease" title="Cerebrovascular disease">cerebrovascular disease</a> being the single biggest killer in Portugal (17%). Portuguese people die 12% less often from cancer than in the Eur-A, but mortality is not declining as rapidly as in the Eur-A. Cancer is more frequent among children as well as among women younger than 44 years. Although lung cancer (slowly increasing among women) and breast cancer (decreasing rapidly) are scarcer, cancer of the cervix and the prostate are more frequent. Portugal has the highest mortality rate for diabetes in the Eur-A, with a sharp increase since the 1980s.</p> 
     <p>Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate" class="mw-redirect">infant mortality rate</a> has dropped sharply since the late 1970s, when 24 of 1000 newborns died in the first year of life. It is now around 2 deaths per a 1000 newborns. This improvement was mainly due to the decrease in neonatal mortality, from 15.5 to 2.4 per 1000 live births.</p> 
     <p>People are usually well informed about their health status, the positive and negative effects of their behaviour on their health and their use of health care services. Yet their perceptions of their health can differ from what administrative and examination-based data show about levels of illness within populations. Thus, survey results based on self-reporting at the household level complement other data on health status and the use of services. Only one third of adults rated their health as good or very good in Portugal (Kasmel et al., 2004). This is the lowest of the Eur-A countries reporting and reflects the relatively adverse situation of the country in terms of mortality and selected morbidity.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Culture of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/260px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg" width="260" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/390px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/520px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2861" data-file-height="1827"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery" title="Jerónimos Monastery">Jerónimos Monastery</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/220px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/330px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/440px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5035" data-file-height="4805"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m_Tower" title="Belém Tower">Belém Tower</a> is a typical example of Portugal's unique 
        <a href="/wiki/Manueline" title="Manueline">Manueline</a> architecture.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal has developed a specific culture while being influenced by various civilizations that have crossed the Mediterranean and the European continent, or were introduced when it played an active role during the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_Age_of_Discovery" title="Portugal in the Age of Discovery" class="mw-redirect">Age of Discovery</a>. In the 1990s and 2000s (decade), Portugal modernized its public cultural facilities, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Calouste_Gulbenkian_Foundation" title="Calouste Gulbenkian Foundation">Calouste Gulbenkian Foundation</a> established in 1956 in Lisbon.</p> 
     <p>These include the <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m_Cultural_Centre" title="Belém Cultural Centre" class="mw-redirect">Belém Cultural Centre</a> in Lisbon, <a href="/wiki/Serralves_Foundation" title="Serralves Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Serralves Foundation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_M%C3%BAsica" title="Casa da Música">Casa da Música</a>, both in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, as well as new public cultural facilities like municipal libraries and concert halls that were built or renovated in many municipalities across the country. Portugal is home to <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Portugal" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Portugal">fifteen</a> UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>, ranking it <a href="/wiki/Table_of_World_Heritage_Sites_by_country" title="Table of World Heritage Sites by country">8th in Europe and 17th in the world.</a></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Portugal" title="Architecture of Portugal">Architecture of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Traditional architecture is distinctive and include the <a href="/wiki/Manueline" title="Manueline">Manueline</a>, also known as Portuguese late Gothic, a sumptuous, composite Portuguese style of architectural ornamentation of the first decades of the 16th century. A 20th-century interpretation of traditional architecture, <a href="/wiki/Soft_Portuguese_style" title="Soft Portuguese style">Soft Portuguese style</a>, appears extensively in major cities, especially Lisbon. Modern Portugal has given the world renowned architects like <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Souto_de_Moura" title="Eduardo Souto de Moura">Eduardo Souto de Moura</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Siza_Vieira" title="Álvaro Siza Vieira">Álvaro Siza Vieira</a> (both <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_Prize" title="Pritzker Prize" class="mw-redirect">Pritzker Prize</a> winners) and <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Byrne" title="Gonçalo Byrne">Gonçalo Byrne</a>. In Portugal <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Taveira" title="Tomás Taveira">Tomás Taveira</a> is also noteworthy, particularly for stadium design.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Portugal" title="Cinema of Portugal">Cinema of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Portugal" title="Cinema of Portugal">Portuguese cinema</a> has a long tradition, reaching back to the birth of the medium in the late 19th century. Portuguese film directors such as <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Duarte" title="Arthur Duarte">Arthur Duarte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Lopes_Ribeiro" title="António Lopes Ribeiro">António Lopes Ribeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Reis" title="António Reis">António Reis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Costa" title="Pedro Costa">Pedro Costa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manoel_de_Oliveira" title="Manoel de Oliveira">Manoel de Oliveira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_C%C3%A9sar_Monteiro" title="João César Monteiro">João César Monteiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio-Pedro_Vasconcelos" title="António-Pedro Vasconcelos">António-Pedro Vasconcelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lopes_(filmmaker)" title="Fernando Lopes (filmmaker)">Fernando Lopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Botelho" title="João Botelho">João Botelho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonel_Vieira" title="Leonel Vieira">Leonel Vieira</a>, are among those that gained notability. Noted Portuguese film actors include <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_de_Almeida" title="Joaquim de Almeida">Joaquim de Almeida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Ruah" title="Daniela Ruah">Daniela Ruah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_de_Medeiros" title="Maria de Medeiros">Maria de Medeiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Infante" title="Diogo Infante">Diogo Infante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soraia_Chaves" title="Soraia Chaves">Soraia Chaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ribeirinho" title="Ribeirinho">Ribeirinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BAcia_Moniz" title="Lúcia Moniz">Lúcia Moniz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Morgado" title="Diogo Morgado">Diogo Morgado</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_literature" title="Portuguese literature">Portuguese literature</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px"> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cam%C3%B5es,_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg/100px-Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg" width="100" height="112" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg/150px-Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg/200px-Cam%C3%B5es%2C_por_Fern%C3%A3o_Gomes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="714"></a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Fernando-pessoa1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Fernando-pessoa1.jpg/100px-Fernando-pessoa1.jpg" width="100" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Fernando-pessoa1.jpg/150px-Fernando-pessoa1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Fernando-pessoa1.jpg/200px-Fernando-pessoa1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="351" data-file-height="387"></a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JSJoseSaramago.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/JSJoseSaramago.jpg/100px-JSJoseSaramago.jpg" width="100" height="78" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/JSJoseSaramago.jpg/150px-JSJoseSaramago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/JSJoseSaramago.jpg/200px-JSJoseSaramago.jpg 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="249"></a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="clear:left"></div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
        <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Luís de Camões">Luís de Camões</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Saramago" title="José Saramago">José Saramago</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portuguese literature, one of the earliest Western literatures, developed through text as well as song. Until 1350, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-Galician" title="Portuguese-Galician" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese-Galician</a> <a href="/wiki/Troubadour" title="Troubadour">troubadours</a> spread their literary influence to most of the Iberian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gil_Vicente" title="Gil Vicente">Gil Vicente</a> (c. 1465–c. 1536), was one of the founders of both Portuguese and Spanish dramatic traditions.</p> 
     <p>Adventurer and poet <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Luís de Camões">Luís de Camões</a> (c. 1524–1580) wrote the epic poem <i>"Os Lusíadas"</i> (<a href="/wiki/The_Lusiads" title="The Lusiads" class="mw-redirect">The Lusiads</a>), with <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a> as his main influence.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-156">[155]</a></sup> Modern Portuguese poetry is rooted in neoclassic and contemporary styles, as exemplified by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a> (1888–1935). Modern Portuguese literature is represented by authors such as <a href="/wiki/Almeida_Garrett" title="Almeida Garrett">Almeida Garrett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Castelo_Branco" title="Camilo Castelo Branco">Camilo Castelo Branco</a>, <a href="/wiki/E%C3%A7a_de_Queiroz" title="Eça de Queiroz" class="mw-redirect">Eça de Queiroz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_de_Mello_Breyner_Andresen" title="Sophia de Mello Breyner Andresen">Sophia de Mello Breyner Andresen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Lobo_Antunes" title="António Lobo Antunes">António Lobo Antunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Torga" title="Miguel Torga">Miguel Torga</a>. Particularly popular and distinguished is <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Saramago" title="José Saramago">José Saramago</a>, recipient of the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_cuisine" title="Portuguese cuisine">Portuguese cuisine</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_wine" title="Portuguese wine">Portuguese wine</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg/220px-Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg/330px-Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg/440px-Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1596" data-file-height="1375"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pastel_de_Nata_Guangzhou_China.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Pastel_de_nata" title="Pastel de nata"><i>Pastéis de nata</i></a> from one of the specialized bakeries in 
        <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Porto.Grahams02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Porto.Grahams02.jpg/220px-Porto.Grahams02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Porto.Grahams02.jpg/330px-Porto.Grahams02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Porto.Grahams02.jpg/440px-Porto.Grahams02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Porto.Grahams02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Wine_tasting" title="Wine tasting">Tasting</a> room of 
        <a href="/wiki/Port_wine" title="Port wine">port wine</a> in a 
        <a href="/wiki/Wine_cellar" title="Wine cellar">wine cellar</a> of a producer
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portuguese cuisine is diverse. The Portuguese consume a lot of dry <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a></i> in Portuguese), for which there are hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau#Bacalhau_dishes" title="Bacalhau">recipes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> There are more than enough <i><a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a></i> dishes for each day of the year. Two other popular fish recipes are grilled <a href="/wiki/Sardines" title="Sardines" class="mw-redirect">sardines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caldeirada" title="Caldeirada">caldeirada</a>, a potato-based <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stew</a> that can be made from several types of fish. Typical Portuguese meat recipes, that may be made out of beef, pork, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_sheep" title="Domestic sheep" class="mw-redirect">lamb</a>, or chicken, include <i><a href="/wiki/Cozido_%C3%A0_portuguesa" title="Cozido à portuguesa" class="mw-redirect">cozido à portuguesa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">feijoada</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Frango_de_churrasco" title="Frango de churrasco" class="mw-redirect">frango de churrasco</a></i>, <i>leitão</i> (roast <a href="/wiki/Suckling_pig" title="Suckling pig">suckling pig</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Carne_de_porco_%C3%A0_alentejana" title="Carne de porco à alentejana">carne de porco à alentejana</a></i>. A very popular northern dish is the arroz de sarrabulho (rice stewed in pigs blood) or the arroz de cabidela (rice and chickens meat stewed in chickens blood).</p> 
     <p>Typical fast food dishes include the <a href="/wiki/Francesinha" title="Francesinha">Francesinha</a> (Frenchie) from Porto, and <i>bifanas</i> (grilled pork) or <i>prego</i> (grilled beef) <a href="/wiki/Sandwich" title="Sandwich">sandwiches</a>, which are well known around the country. The Portuguese art of <a href="/wiki/Pastry" title="Pastry">pastry</a> has its origins in the many <a href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval" class="mw-redirect">medieval</a> Catholic monasteries spread widely across the country. These monasteries, using very few ingredients (mostly almonds, flour, eggs and some liquor), managed to create a spectacular wide range of different pastries, of which <a href="/wiki/Past%C3%A9is_de_Bel%C3%A9m" title="Pastéis de Belém" class="mw-redirect">pastéis de Belém</a> (or <i>pastéis de nata</i>) originally from Lisbon, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ovos_moles" title="Ovos moles" class="mw-redirect">ovos moles</a></i> from Aveiro are examples. Portuguese cuisine is very diverse, with different regions having their own traditional dishes. The Portuguese have a culture of good food, and throughout the country there are myriads of good restaurants and typical small <i>tasquinhas</i>.</p> 
     <p>Portuguese wines have enjoyed international recognition since the times of the Romans, who associated Portugal with their god <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Bacchus</a>. Today, the country is known by wine lovers and its wines have won several international prizes. Some of the best Portuguese wines are: <a href="/wiki/Vinho_Verde" title="Vinho Verde">Vinho Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_Alvarinho" title="Vinho Alvarinho" class="mw-redirect">Vinho Alvarinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_Douro" title="Vinho do Douro" class="mw-redirect">Vinho do Douro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_Alentejo" title="Vinho do Alentejo" class="mw-redirect">Vinho do Alentejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_D%C3%A3o" title="Vinho do Dão" class="mw-redirect">Vinho do Dão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_da_Bairrada" title="Vinho da Bairrada" class="mw-redirect">Vinho da Bairrada</a> and the sweet: <a href="/wiki/Port_Wine" title="Port Wine" class="mw-redirect">Port Wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Wine" title="Madeira Wine" class="mw-redirect">Madeira Wine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moscatel" title="Moscatel" class="mw-redirect">Moscatel</a> from <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">Setúbal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Favaios" title="Favaios">Favaios</a>. Port and Madeira are particularly appreciated in a wide range of places around the world.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Portugal" title="Music of Portugal">Music of Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg/300px-1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg/450px-1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg/600px-1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3543" data-file-height="2362"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:1-Casa_da_Musica-exterior_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_M%C3%BAsica" title="Casa da Música">Casa da Música</a>, a concert hall in 
        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Portugal" title="Music of Portugal">Portuguese music</a> encompasses a wide variety of genres. The most renowned is <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a>, a melancholy urban music originated in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, usually associated with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_guitar" title="Portuguese guitar">Portuguese guitar</a> and <i>saudade</i>, or longing. <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_fado" title="Coimbra fado" class="mw-redirect">Coimbra fado</a>, a unique type of "serenading" fado, is also noteworthy. Internationally notable performers include <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A1lia_Rodrigues" title="Amália Rodrigues">Amália Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Paredes" title="Carlos Paredes">Carlos Paredes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Afonso" title="José Afonso" class="mw-redirect">José Afonso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariza" title="Mariza">Mariza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_do_Carmo" title="Carlos do Carmo">Carlos do Carmo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Chainho" title="António Chainho">António Chainho</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%ADsia" title="Mísia">Mísia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madredeus" title="Madredeus">Madredeus</a>.</p> 
     <p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">Folk</a>, the Portuguese listen to pop and other types of modern music, particularly from North America and the United Kingdom, as well as a wide range of Portuguese, Caribbean and Brazilian artists and bands. Artists with international recognition include <a href="/wiki/Dulce_Pontes" title="Dulce Pontes">Dulce Pontes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moonspell" title="Moonspell">Moonspell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buraka_Som_Sistema" title="Buraka Som Sistema">Buraka Som Sistema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blasted_Mechanism" title="Blasted Mechanism">Blasted Mechanism</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Gift_(band)" title="The Gift (band)">The Gift</a>, with the two latter being nominees for a <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award" title="MTV Europe Music Award" class="mw-redirect">MTV Europe Music Award</a>.</p> 
     <p>Portugal has several summer music festivals, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_Sudoeste" title="Festival Sudoeste">Festival Sudoeste</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Zambujeira_do_Mar" title="Zambujeira do Mar">Zambujeira do Mar</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_de_Paredes_de_Coura" title="Festival de Paredes de Coura" class="mw-redirect">Festival de Paredes de Coura</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Paredes_de_Coura" title="Paredes de Coura">Paredes de Coura</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_Vilar_de_Mouros" title="Festival Vilar de Mouros" class="mw-redirect">Festival Vilar de Mouros</a></i> near <a href="/wiki/Caminha" title="Caminha">Caminha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boom_Festival" title="Boom Festival">Boom Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Idanha-a-Nova_Municipality" title="Idanha-a-Nova Municipality" class="mw-redirect">Idanha-a-Nova Municipality</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Optimus_Alive!" title="Optimus Alive!" class="mw-redirect">Optimus Alive!</a></i>, <i>Sumol Summer Fest</i> in <a href="/wiki/Ericeira" title="Ericeira">Ericeira</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Lisboa.2C_Portugal.2C_and_Madrid.2C_Spain" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio Lisboa</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Bock_Super_Rock" title="Super Bock Super Rock">Super Bock Super Rock</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Lisbon" title="Greater Lisbon" class="mw-redirect">Greater Lisbon</a>. Out of the summer season, Portugal has a large number of festivals, designed more to an urban audience, like Flowfest or Hip Hop Porto. Furthermore, one of the largest international <a href="/wiki/Goa_trance" title="Goa trance">Goa trance</a> festivals takes place in central Portugal every two years, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://boomfestival.org/boom2012/">Boom Festival</a>, that is also the only festival in Portugal to win international awards: European Festival Award 2010 – Green'n'Clean Festival of the Year and the Greener Festival Award Outstanding 2008 and 2010. There is also the student festivals of <i><a href="/wiki/Queima_das_Fitas" title="Queima das Fitas">Queima das Fitas</a></i> are major events in a number of cities across Portugal. In 2005, Portugal held the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Pavilh%C3%A3o_Atl%C3%A2ntico" title="Pavilhão Atlântico" class="mw-redirect">Pavilhão Atlântico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</p> 
     <p>In the classical music domain, Portugal is represented by names as the pianists <a href="/wiki/Artur_Pizarro" title="Artur Pizarro">Artur Pizarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Jo%C3%A3o_Pires" title="Maria João Pires">Maria João Pires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sequeira_Costa" title="Sequeira Costa">Sequeira Costa</a>, the violinists Carlos Damas, <a href="/wiki/Gerardo_Ribeiro" title="Gerardo Ribeiro">Gerardo Ribeiro</a> and in the past by the great cellist <a href="/wiki/Guilhermina_Suggia" title="Guilhermina Suggia">Guilhermina Suggia</a>. Notable composers include <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vianna_da_Motta" title="José Vianna da Motta">José Vianna da Motta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Seixas" title="Carlos Seixas">Carlos Seixas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Domingos_Bomtempo" title="João Domingos Bomtempo">João Domingos Bomtempo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_Sousa_Carvalho" title="João de Sousa Carvalho">João de Sousa Carvalho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Freitas_Branco" title="Luís de Freitas Branco">Luís de Freitas Branco</a> and his student <a href="/wiki/Joly_Braga_Santos" title="Joly Braga Santos">Joly Braga Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lopes-Gra%C3%A7a" title="Fernando Lopes-Graça">Fernando Lopes-Graça</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Nunes" title="Emmanuel Nunes">Emmanuel Nunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9rgio_Azevedo" title="Sérgio Azevedo">Sérgio Azevedo</a>. Similarly, contemporary composers such as Nuno Malo and Miguel d'Oliveira have achieved some international success writing <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">original music for film and television</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg/170px-Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg" width="170" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg/255px-Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg/340px-Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1250"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Painel_dos_Infantes_Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves_circa_1460.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Panels" title="Saint Vincent Panels">Saint Vincent Panels</a>, attributed to 
        <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves" title="Nuno Gonçalves">Nuno Gonçalves</a>, a 
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a> artist.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_artists" title="List of Portuguese artists">rich history in painting</a>. The first well-known painters date back to the 15th century&nbsp;– like <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves" title="Nuno Gonçalves">Nuno Gonçalves</a>&nbsp;– were part of the Gothic painting period. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Malhoa" title="José Malhoa">José Malhoa</a>, known for his work <i>Fado</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Columbano_Bordalo_Pinheiro" title="Columbano Bordalo Pinheiro">Columbano Bordalo Pinheiro</a> (who painted the portraits of <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Braga" title="Teófilo Braga">Teófilo Braga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antero_de_Quental" title="Antero de Quental">Antero de Quental</a>) were both references in <a href="/wiki/Naturalist_school_of_painting" title="Naturalist school of painting" class="mw-redirect">naturalist painting</a>.</p> 
     <p>The 20th century saw the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a>, and along with it came the most prominent Portuguese painters: <a href="/wiki/Amadeo_de_Souza-Cardoso" title="Amadeo de Souza-Cardoso" class="mw-redirect">Amadeo de Souza-Cardoso</a>, who was heavily influenced by French painters, particularly by the <a href="/wiki/Delaunays" title="Delaunays" class="mw-redirect">Delaunays</a>. Among his best-known works is <i>Canção Popular a Russa e o Fígaro</i>. Another great modernist painters/writers were <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Botelho" title="Carlos Botelho">Carlos Botelho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almada_Negreiros" title="Almada Negreiros" class="mw-redirect">Almada Negreiros</a>, friend to the poet <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a>, who painted his (Pessoa's) portrait. He was deeply influenced by both <a href="/wiki/Cubist" title="Cubist" class="mw-redirect">Cubist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Futurism_(art)" title="Futurism (art)" class="mw-redirect">Futurist</a> trends. Prominent international figures in visual arts nowadays include painters <a href="/wiki/Vieira_da_Silva" title="Vieira da Silva" class="mw-redirect">Vieira da Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_Pomar" title="Júlio Pomar">Júlio Pomar</a>, Helena Almeida, <a href="/wiki/Joana_Vasconcelos" title="Joana Vasconcelos">Joana Vasconcelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juli%C3%A3o_Sarmento" title="Julião Sarmento">Julião Sarmento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paula_Rego" title="Paula Rego">Paula Rego</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Portugal" title="Sport in Portugal">Sport in Portugal</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/170px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/255px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/340px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg 2x" data-file-width="435" data-file-height="656"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, captain of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal national football team</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Portugal. There are several football competitions ranging from local amateur to world-class professional level. The legendary <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eusébio">Eusébio</a> is still a major symbol of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_football" title="Portuguese football" class="mw-redirect">Portuguese football</a> history. <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Player_of_the_Year" title="FIFA World Player of the Year">FIFA World Player of the Year</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="Luís Figo">Luís Figo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> who won the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d'Or">FIFA Ballon d'Or</a> for 2013 and 2014, are among the numerous examples of other world-class football players born in Portugal and noted worldwide. Portuguese football managers are also noteworthy, with <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Villas-Boas" title="André Villas-Boas">André Villas-Boas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Santos_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Fernando Santos (Portuguese footballer)">Fernando Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Queiroz" title="Carlos Queiroz">Carlos Queiroz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Jos%C3%A9" title="Manuel José" class="mw-redirect">Manuel José</a> among the most renowned.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portuguese national football team</a> has titles in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="FIFA World Youth Championship" class="mw-redirect">FIFA World Youth Championship</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> youth championships. The main national team&nbsp;– <i>Selecção Nacional</i>&nbsp;– finished second in <a href="/wiki/2004_European_Football_Championship" title="2004 European Football Championship" class="mw-redirect">Euro 2004</a> (held in Portugal), reached the third place in the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a>, and reached the fourth place in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, their best results in major competitions to date.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/F.C._Porto" title="F.C. Porto" class="mw-redirect">FC Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">SL Benfica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sporting_C.P." title="Sporting C.P." class="mw-redirect">Sporting CP</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Sports_clubs" title="Sports clubs" class="mw-redirect">sports clubs</a> by popularity and by number of trophies won, often known as "<i>os três grandes</i>" (<a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(Portugal)" title="Big Three (Portugal)">"the big three"</a>). They have won eight titles in the European <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> club competitions, were present in many finals and have been regular contenders in the last stages almost every season. Other than football, many Portuguese sports clubs, including the "big three", compete in several other sports events with a varying level of success and popularity, these may include <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">roller hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball" class="mw-redirect">handball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Football_Federation" title="Portuguese Football Federation">Portuguese Football Federation</a> (FPF) &nbsp;– <i>Federação Portuguesa de Futebol</i>&nbsp;– annually hosts the <a href="/wiki/Algarve_Cup" title="Algarve Cup">Algarve Cup</a>, a prestigious <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women's association football">women`s football</a> tournament that has been celebrated in the Algarvian part of Portugal.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg/300px-Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg/450px-Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg/600px-Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Euro2004OpeningCeremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The opening ceremony of the 
        <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">UEFA Euro 2004</a> at 
        <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Drag%C3%A3o" title="Estádio do Dragão">Estádio do Dragão</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Portugal has a successful roller hockey team, with 15 <a href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">world titles</a> and 20 <a href="/wiki/CERH_European_Roller_Hockey_Championship" title="CERH European Roller Hockey Championship">European titles</a>, making it the country with the most wins in both competitions. The most successful Portuguese roller hockey clubs in the history of European championships are <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto_(rink_hockey)" title="FC Porto (rink hockey)" class="mw-redirect">Futebol Clube do Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/SL_Benfica_(rink_hockey)" title="SL Benfica (rink hockey)" class="mw-redirect">Sport Lisboa e Benfica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Portugal_(roller_hockey)" title="Sporting Clube de Portugal (roller hockey)">Sporting Clube de Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%93quei_de_Barcelos" title="Óquei de Barcelos" class="mw-redirect">Óquei de Barcelos</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_rugby_union_team" title="Portugal national rugby union team">Portuguese national rugby union team</a> made a dramatic qualification into the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a> and became the first all amateur team to qualify for the World Cup since the dawn of the professional era. The <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_rugby_union_team_(sevens)" title="Portugal national rugby union team (sevens)">Portuguese national rugby sevens team</a> has performed well, becoming one of the strongest teams in Europe, and proved their status as European champions in several occasions.</p> 
     <p>In <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)" class="mw-redirect">athletics</a>, the Portuguese have won a number of gold, silver and bronze medals in the European, World and Olympic Games competitions. <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">Cycling</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Volta_a_Portugal" title="Volta a Portugal">Volta a Portugal</a> being the most important race, is also a popular sports event and include professional cycling teams such as W52-<i>FC Porto</i>-Porto Canal, <a href="/wiki/SL_Benfica_(cycling_team)" title="SL Benfica (cycling team)" class="mw-redirect">Sport Lisboa e Benfica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boavista_(cycling_team)" title="Boavista (cycling team)" class="mw-redirect">Boavista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Ciclismo_de_Tavira" title="Clube de Ciclismo de Tavira" class="mw-redirect">Clube de Ciclismo de Tavira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%A3o_Ciclista_da_Maia" title="União Ciclista da Maia">União Ciclista da Maia</a>.</p> 
     <p>The country has also achieved notable performances in sports like <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kitesurf" title="Kitesurf" class="mw-redirect">kitesurf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>, sailing, <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>, shooting, <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windsurf" title="Windsurf" class="mw-redirect">windsurf</a>, owning several European and world titles. The <a href="/wiki/Paralympic" title="Paralympic" class="mw-redirect">paralympic</a> athletes have also conquered many medals in sports like swimming, <a href="/wiki/Boccia" title="Boccia">boccia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>.</p> 
     <p>In motorsport, Portugal is internationally noted for the <a href="/wiki/Rally_of_Portugal" title="Rally of Portugal" class="mw-redirect">Rally of Portugal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Estoril_Circuit" title="Estoril Circuit" class="mw-redirect">Estoril</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algarve_Circuit" title="Algarve Circuit" class="mw-redirect">Algarve Circuits</a> and the revived <a href="/wiki/Porto_Street_Circuit" title="Porto Street Circuit" class="mw-redirect">Porto Street Circuit</a> which holds a stage of the WTCC every two years, as well as for a number of internationally noted pilots in varied <a href="/wiki/Motorsports" title="Motorsports" class="mw-redirect">motorsports</a>.</p> 
     <p>In equestrian sports, Portugal won the only Horseball-Pato World Championship (in 2006), achieved the third position in the First <a href="/wiki/Horseball" title="Horseball">Horseball</a> World Cup (organized in Ponte de Lima, Portugal, in 2008), and has achieved several victories in the European <a href="/wiki/Working_Equitation" title="Working Equitation" class="mw-redirect">Working Equitation</a> Championship.</p> 
     <p>In water sports, Portugal has two major sports: <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>. Northern Portugal has its own original <a href="/wiki/Martial_art" title="Martial art" class="mw-redirect">martial art</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jogo_do_Pau" title="Jogo do Pau" class="mw-redirect">Jogo do Pau</a></i>, in which the fighters use staffs to confront one or several opponents. Other popular sport-related recreational outdoor activities with thousands of enthusiasts nationwide include <a href="/wiki/Airsoft" title="Airsoft">airsoft</a>, fishing, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, hiking, hunting and <a href="/wiki/Orienteering" title="Orienteering">orienteering</a>.</p> 
     <p>Portugal is widely acknowledged as one of the world's best <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> destinations it has received several awards by the World Golf Awards. It´s great weather allows you to play all year round, from north to south, in the countryside or by the sea. Discover the outstanding of the Portuguese Golf Destination in one of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.golftourportugal.com">leading websites of Portugal.</a></p>

       <li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://digital.csic.es/bitstream/10261/9858/1/1812Cadiz.pdf">Peña,Lorenzo. Un puente jurídico entre Iberoamérica y Europa:la Constitución española de 1812. Instituto de Filosofía del CSIC</a></span> 
        <blockquote class="templatequote"> 
         <p><span class="reference-text">The first thing there is to understand is that in a good measure, the Courts of Cadiz created a new state, the Spanish state.[...]there had never been a proclamation of a Kingdom of Spain, so that difficulties always arose upon the legal value of the very frequent references to 'Spain' in the legal texts of the sixteenth, seventeenth and eighteenth centuries. The Spanish sovereigns had always refused the advice [...] in the sense of establishing a United Kingdom of Spain, preferring to see themselves as vertices of converging scattered kingdoms, at least in theory. Even the Napoleonic Bayonne Constitution of 1808 did not proclaim a kingdom of Spain, but a 'Crown of Spain and the Indies'. On the other hand, 'Spain' was merely a geographical name, a simple romance version of 'Hispania',whereby its use, in principle, should not have to go beyond the designations ‘Galia’,‘Germania’[...]</span></p> 
        </blockquote> </li>

Officially the Republic of China, participates as "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Separate Customs Territory of Taiwan, Penghu, Kinmen and Matsu</a>", and "Chinese Taipei" in short.</span></p>
